<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:0px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background001.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:246.41px;top:67.32px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">Religion and the Absurd:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:158.78px;top:85.34px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">A Skeptic’s View of Judaeo-Christian Scripture and Tradition</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:274.01px;top:103.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Introduction:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:117.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Having been raised as a Catholic, I was aghast when, as a grade-schooler who took my faith very</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:131.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">seriously, I was told that the prohibition on eating meat on Fridays had been lifted. What?! Can</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:145.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">they do that?! Says who?! After that, the holy cows starting falling like snowflakes: the Mass was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:159.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">now to be in English, and breakfast could be taken before communion! Where would it end? And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:173.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">where did all those rules come from in the first place? Slowly I began to realize that they were</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:187.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invented by old priests in an incense-filled room. That’s when I started to question everything else.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:201.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Having made the fateful decision to read the Bible myself, I became ever more dubious as to the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:215.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">authority and intentions of churches and religion in general.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:233.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In order that other persons of an open mind</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:247.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">might make informed decisions regarding</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:261.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religion, I have documented some of my</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:275.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">surprising discoveries, such as that Jesus and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:289.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul differed widely on the qualifications for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:303.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">salvation, and that churches, in self-interest,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:317.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">chose Paul over Jesus and his brother James.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:335.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">People, however, will believe what they want to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:349.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">believe, evidence notwithstanding, so I don’t</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:363.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">expect to change anyone’s mind. I am resigned</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:377.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to being both misread and condemned by the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:391.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">same self-interested church zealots who threw</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:405.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">over Jesus for Paul. If, though, you are of an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:419.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">open mind, please peruse these articles and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:434.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">come to your own conclusions.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:448.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The articles are divided into four sections: first, a chronological investigation of religious views of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:462.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Scripture; second, an investigation of the real and mythical Jesus with selections from the Gospel</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:476.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">according to Matthew; third, an analysis of motives for belief; and fourth, a list of apocalyptic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:490.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(need I say, incorrect) predictions of the end of the world.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:508.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">These articles are the fruit of a collective effort and remain so. I take responsibility for compiling and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:522.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">editing the contributions. If someone has an insight into one of the subjects treated herein or feels a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:536.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mistake has been made, please enlighten us.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:556.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">1</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:802px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background002.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:276.53px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Definitions:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:81.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Religion - a set of doctrines which requires faith in metaphysical phenomena (i.e., gods, miracles,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:95.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">afterlife, power of prayer, etc.). If a set of doctrines does not require faith, then it does not qualify</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:109.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as a religion, but only as a philosophy. Many religions claim a mutually exclusive right to Truth -</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:123.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">they maintain that their religion is right, and all others are wrong - while others are more inclusive.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Absurd - a phenomenon which defies reasonable explanation.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Soeren Kierkegaard (hereafter K), whose Fear</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and Trembling posits acceptance of the Absurd as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:183.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prerequisite for faith, uses the example of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Abraham’s unquestioning resolve to kill his son</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Isaac based only upon the command of a voice in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">his head that he identified as God. K considers</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">this action Absurd because it defies logic and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">social custom. Christian dogma, according to K,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">embodies paradoxes which are offensive to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reason. (Indeed, were someone today to say</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that he intended to kill his child because a voice</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in his head had instructed him to, we too might</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:323.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">react with Fear and Trembling!) There are two</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:337.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">attitudes one can adopt to this assertion: viz.,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">one can take K’s leap of faith and believe, or one</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">can doubt. What one may not do, according to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:379.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">K, is have faith by virtue of reason. If one chooses</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:393.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faith, one must suspend reason. In fact one</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">must believe by virtue of the Absurd.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:421.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">K notwithstanding, A rational individual should apply the same objectivity to her own beliefs as she</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:436.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">would to those of another, for who would not agree that the believers in other gods are wrong?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:450.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Spirituality or Religion? I personally am not an atheist - it seems self-evident to me that there is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:464.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">something behind the wondrous universe in which we live, and that intuitive knowledge can lead to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:478.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">insights into its nature - but I am wary of pre-scientific legends that later claim factual credibility</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:492.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(inerrancy). I object to the presentation of religion as based in fact and science, and I feel there is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:506.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">copious evidence that exposes these stories as myth or legend. I have, however, included rebuttals</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to my assertions and I welcome readers to offer their own rebuttals where they think I have erred.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Religion performs useful social functions and is cherished by a great many people, but is also</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:548.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">responsible for enormous monstrosities in human history. Like a rifle which may be used either for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:562.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hunting and for personal protection or for mass murder, so religion in the right hands may be a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:576.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">productive element in society, but in the wrong hands a powerful destructive force. Perhaps the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:590.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">greatest flaws in religion are that it teaches people from earliest youth to reject objectivity and to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:604.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">blindly follow fairy tales, and that it depersonalizes judgment so that, for example, an otherwise</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:618.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">civilized person might kill his own child on a whim.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:638.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">2</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:1604px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background003.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:166.94px;top:73.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Evolution of the Relationship between Religion and Science</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:87.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1. The Primitive Period</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:101.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In the beginning, all was mysterious, terrifying,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:115.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and wonderful. Man did not understand the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">origin of earthquakes, lightning, or how the sun</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">got from the west back to the east for sunrise</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the next morning. Why did plants grow? Why</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">did people get sick and die? People were</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">desperate for answers, which they found</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">according to what seemed most reasonable.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Wherever a phenomenon defied natural</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">explanation, some supernatural agency was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">presumed. Further, people desperately wanted</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to be able to control these phenomena and so</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">instituted sacrifices and prayers in the belief</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that these actions could influence the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">appropriate deities. At this point religion and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">science were synonymous.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:331.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2.The Growth of Science</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:345.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">As knowledge of the physical world increasingly showed non-spiritual causes of phenomena,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:359.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">entrenched religious authorities threatened with a diminution in the scope of their influence reacted</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:373.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">forcefully against the “impious” assertions of secular knowledge.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:393.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3.The  Current State of Affairs</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">As science continues to advance our understanding of the world and ourselves, the original rationale</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:421.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for religion itself is progressively undermined. Confronted with refutations of core beliefs,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:435.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religionists have responded in a variety of ways: some modify their beliefs to accommodate science,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:449.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">while some seek alternate realities. Even science has been posited as a religion of sorts by some</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:463.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">apologists of faith. In some cases, the entrenched interests of organized religion and social</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:478.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conservatism have instituted a war against science itself and the public schools that bring unwelcome</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:492.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ideas into their communities.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:512.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4. The persistence of superstition (i.e., faith, prayer, miracles, etc.)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Why do parents encourage their children to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:540.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">believe in obvious falsehoods: Santa Claus,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">turning water to wine, the “Virgin” Mary, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:568.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gift of tongues? Why do people persist in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:582.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">belief that prayers are efficacious? Did the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:596.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">people whose house was hit by the tornado not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:610.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">pray hard enough? Besides, isn’t a prayer</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:624.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">simply a request that God change his Divine</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:638.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Plan in order to accommodate one’s personal</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:652.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">desire? Isn’t it a rejection of “thy will be done”?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:666.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">We will investigate these questions below.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:686.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">3</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:2406px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background004.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:132.14px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Part One - A Chronological Consideration of Judaeo-Christian Theology</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:201.98px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Historical Overview of pre-Christian Israel:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:99.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The history of the Hebrew people is well documented by outside sources (Egypt, Assyria, Babylon,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:113.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Persia, Greece, Rome) as well as by Jewish historians and Scripture. Absent the mythology, what</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">seems most likely is that the Hebrews migrated from Mesopotamia to the highlands of Canaan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">around 1700 BCE, and brought with them numerous religious myths. Around the time of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Solomon these stories were crystallized in the Scripture by authors known as J (Jehovist) and E</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Elohist), with later additions by D (Deuteronomist), Chron (icler), Prophets, and P (Priests).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David’s kingdom then split into Samaria (Israel) in the north, with a temple at Shiloh served by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Aaronite priests; and Judea in the south, with a temple at Jerusalem served by Zadokite priests.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">There was widespread on-going polytheistic worship of El, Baal, and Asherah, as well as an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">incipient monotheism centered on YHWH (Jehovah), the newly enshrined war-god of Judea.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judean Prophets soon emerged who demanded exclusive worship of YHWH, and their warnings</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the dangers of inclusive Yahwism (worship of other gods along with YHWH) seemed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">vindicated when Samaria fell to Assyria in 722 BCE. At this point D rewrites Scripture to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophesy the fall of Samaria, perpetual Davidic kingship, etc.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In 586 BCE, though, faith in YHWH was tested</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">when Jerusalem was conquered and the Temple</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">destroyed by Babylonians. Judean leaders and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:341.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">priests were removed to Babylon (Babylonian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:355.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Exile), during which time they retooled their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:369.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">theology to account for what had happened.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:383.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">They concluded that YHWH was punishing</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:397.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">them for apostasy (allowing the worship of Baal</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and Asherah - El had already been assimilated</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">into   YHWH)  and   genealogical   impurity</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(intermarriage with the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:442.99px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“unclean” Canaanite</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">women). Their history was rewritten by P and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:468.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Chron to emphasize the myths of Moses, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:482.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Exodus, and a mythic conquest of Canaan.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:498.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">When they returned to Palestine with their new Scriptures and genealogies in hand, these</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:512.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian exiles reclaimed “their” land and imposed a harsh, xenophobic regime of exclusive</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Yahwism. Scripture had been rewritten by these Judean exilic returnees, so it is small wonder that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:540.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">exclusive Yahwism predominates in Scripture at the expense of northern, Samarian inclusivity.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:556.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This did not lead to the liberation of Judea from foreign domination, however. The Babylonians</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:570.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">were followed by the Persians with their Zoroastrian dualism, and then the Greeks, who offered a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:584.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sophisticated individualistic philosophy and a cosmopolitan worldview that appealed to many</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:598.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">affluent Jews. This threat was met by further xenophobic isolation and a stronger sense of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:612.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">identification with mythic Tradition. The failure of their piety to liberate them from foreign</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:626.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">domination, encouraged by Zoroastrian dualism, finally led to the theology of Apocalypticism - the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">belief present both in Daniel and the Gospels - that we are living in an age dominated by evil that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:654.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">can only be saved by direct, imminent divine intervention.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:674.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">4</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:3208px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background005.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:270.41px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Adam and Eve</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Exactly why were Adam and Eve expelled from the Garden of Eden? It’s probably not why you</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">think. The evidence strongly suggests that this story was intended as a myth: a man named Man, a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">woman named Woman, and a talking snake. (All citations are from the King James Version):</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Genesis 2:15 And the LORD God took the man,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and put him into the garden of Eden to dress it</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and to keep it.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:404.59px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">16 And the LORD God</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">commanded the man, saying, Of every tree of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the garden thou mayest freely eat: 17 But of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">tree of the knowledge of good and evil, thou</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shalt not eat of it: for in the day that thou eatest</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thereof thou shalt surely die. …3:1 Now the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">serpent was more subtil than any beast of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">field which the LORD God had made. And he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">said unto the woman, Yea, hath God said, Ye</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shall not eat of every tree of the garden? 2 And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the woman said unto the serpent, We may eat</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the fruit of the trees of the garden:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3 But of the fruit of the tree which is in the midst of the garden, God hath said, Ye shall not eat</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of it, neither shall ye touch it, lest ye die. 4 And the serpent said unto the woman, Ye shall not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">surely die: 5 For God doth know that in the day ye eat thereof, then your eyes shall be opened,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and ye shall be as gods, knowing good and evil. 6 And when the woman saw that the tree was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">good for food, and that it was pleasant to the eyes, and a tree to be desired to make one wise,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">she took of the fruit thereof, and did eat, and gave also unto her husband with her; and he did</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">eat. 7 And the eyes of them both were opened, and they knew that they were naked; and they</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sewed fig leaves together, and made themselves aprons. 8 And they heard the voice of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">LORD God walking in the garden in the cool of the day: and Adam and his wife hid</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">themselves from the presence of the LORD God amongst the trees of the garden. 9 And the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:466.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">LORD God called unto Adam, and said unto him, Where art thou? 10 And he said, I heard</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:480.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thy voice in the garden, and I was afraid, because I was naked; and I hid myself. 11 And he said,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:494.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Who told thee that thou wast naked? Hast thou eaten of the tree, whereof I commanded thee</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:508.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that thou shouldest not eat? 12 And the man said, The woman whom thou gavest to be with me,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:522.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">she gave me of the tree, and I did eat. 13 And the LORD God said unto the woman, What is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:536.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">this that thou hast done? And the woman said, The serpent beguiled me, and I did eat. … 22</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:550.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">And the LORD God said, Behold, the man is become as one of us, to know good and evil: and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:564.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">now, lest he put forth his hand, and take also of the tree of life, and eat, and live for ever: 23</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:578.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Therefore the LORD God sent him forth from the garden of Eden, to till the ground from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:592.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">whence he was taken. 24 So he drove out the man; and he placed at the east of the garden of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:606.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Eden Cherubims, and a flaming sword which turned every way, to keep the way of the tree of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:620.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">life.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:636.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">So Adam and Eve didn’t die the day they ate the fruit, as God had said they would; they could</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:650.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have lived forever, had they eaten the fruit of the Tree of Life; and after they had become as gods</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:664.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">God banished them from Eden to prevent their immortality. Not the Sunday school version.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:4010px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">

<div style="position:absolute;left:277.85px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Noah’s Ark</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In the story of the Flood, P (the Priestly source) and J (the Yahwist source) differ in the number of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">animals to be brought onboard, and how long the flood lasted. Here the two stories are separated:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:113.30px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">“P” Flood Numbers</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">6:19 And of every living thing of all flesh, </span><span class="cls_022">two</span><span class="cls_003"> of every sort shalt thou bring into the ark, to keep</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">them alive with thee; they shall be male and female. 20 Of fowls after their kind, and of cattle after</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">their kind, of every creeping thing of the earth after his kind, </span><span class="cls_022">two</span><span class="cls_003"> of every sort shall come unto thee,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to keep them alive...7:11 </span><span class="cls_022">In the six hundredth year of Noah's life, in the second month, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">seventeenth day of the month</span><span class="cls_003">, the same day were all the fountains of the great deep broken up, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the windows of heaven were opened. 24 And the waters prevailed upon the earth an </span><span class="cls_022">hundred and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">fifty days</span><span class="cls_003">… 8:3 and after the end of the </span><span class="cls_022">hundred and fifty days</span><span class="cls_003"> the waters were abated. 4 And the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ark rested in the seventh month, on the seventeenth day of the month, upon the mountains of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ararat. 5 And the waters decreased continually until the tenth month: in the tenth month, on the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">first day of the month, were the tops of the mountains seen. 13 And it came to pass in the six</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hundredth and first year, in the first month, the first day of the month, the waters were dried up</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from off the earth: 14 And in the </span><span class="cls_022">second month, on the seven and twentieth day of the month, was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:297.65px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">the earth dried</span><span class="cls_003">.  (=376 days)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“</span><span class="cls_022">J” Flood Numbers</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:329.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">7:2 Of every clean beast thou shalt take to thee</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:343.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by </span><span class="cls_022">sevens</span><span class="cls_003">, the male and his female: and of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">beasts that are not clean by </span><span class="cls_022">two</span><span class="cls_003">, the male and his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">female. 3 Of fowls also of the air by </span><span class="cls_022">sevens,</span><span class="cls_003"> the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">male and the female; to keep seed alive upon the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:399.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">face of all the earth. 4 For yet seven days, and I</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:413.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">will cause it to rain upon the earth </span><span class="cls_022">forty days</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:427.99px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">and forty nights…</span><span class="cls_003"> 8:6 And it came to pass at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:442.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the </span><span class="cls_022">end of forty days,</span><span class="cls_003"> that Noah opened the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:456.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">window of the ark which he had made:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">7 And he sent forth a raven, which went forth to and fro, until the waters were dried up from off</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:486.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the earth. 8 Also he sent forth a dove from him, to see if the waters were abated from off the face</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the ground; 9 But the dove found no rest for the sole of her foot, and she returned unto him into</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the ark, for the waters were on the face of the whole earth: then he put forth his hand, and took her,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and pulled her in unto him into the ark. 10 And he stayed </span><span class="cls_022">yet other seven days</span><span class="cls_003">; and again he sent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:542.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">forth the dove out of the ark; 11 And the dove came in to him in the evening; and, lo, in her mouth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:556.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was an olive leaf pluckt off: so Noah knew that the waters were abated from off the earth. 12 And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:570.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he stayed </span><span class="cls_022">yet other seven days</span><span class="cls_003">; and sent forth the dove; which returned not again unto him any</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:584.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">more. 13… and Noah removed the covering of the ark, and looked, and, behold, the face of </span><span class="cls_022">the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:598.30px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">ground was dry</span><span class="cls_003">. (= 61 days, calculating seven days after the raven, because in verse 10 he says</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:612.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“other” = “another” seven days; otherwise, 54 days.)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.38px;top:629.98px" class="cls_023"><span class="cls_023">Rebuttal: The mediaeval Jewish commentator, Rashi, explains that what scripture means is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:643.90px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that a pair of all “unclean” - ritually impure - animals is meant and 7 pair of ritually “clean”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:658.06px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">animals.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:679.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">6</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:4812px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background007.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:264.89px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Joseph Story</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Even more noteworthy is the weaving together of the J (southern Yahwist source) and E (the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">northern Elohist source) strands of the Joseph story, in which the two diverge markedly. Note</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that the southern source prefers Judah and the northern source prefers Reuben, the first-born, in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the leadership role:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:145.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In brief, Joseph was hated by his brothers, who</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:159.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">one day sold him and/or put him into a well and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:173.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faked his death. Joseph ends up in Egypt and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:187.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">works his way up from slave to valued advisor</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:201.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to the Prime Minister for the Pharaoh. His</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brothers come to Egypt during a famine and are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:229.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brought before him.  The do not recognize him.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:243.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He accuses them of being spies and demands</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:257.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that they bring his father and youngest brother</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:271.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">back. When they return, he reveals his identity</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:285.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and is reunified with his family. They stay in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Egypt.  The  father  Jacob</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:458.48px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Israel)  dies,  is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">embalmed and buried in Canaan. Joseph dies, is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">embalmed and buried in Egypt. The family</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:319.01px;top:341.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">stays in Egypt until the Exodus.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">There are numerous inconsistencies in the story, which are outlined below, along with a rebuttal to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the claim of inconsistency according to the mediaeval Jewish scholar Rashi.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:391.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in “J” (Genesis)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:360.07px;top:391.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in “E” (Genesis)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Who saves Joseph?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judah (37:26)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:360.07px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Reuben (37:21)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joseph is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sold to Ishmaelites (37:25,27)  found by Midianites (37:28)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brought to Egypt by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ishmaelites (37:28)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:360.07px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Midianites (37:36)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:455.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brothers’ bags opened</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:455.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">at the inn (42:9)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:360.07px;top:455.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">at home (42:35)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">surety for Benjamin</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:216.05px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judah (43:3)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:360.07px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Reuben (42:37)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:489.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Rebuttal: Reuben advised not shedding Joseph’s blood but rather to throw him into the pit</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:503.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with the idea perhaps of rescuing Joseph later. After Joseph was thrown into the pit, Judah</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:517.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">suggested that Joseph could be saved by selling him to the caravan of traders.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:535.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ishmaelites vs Midianites: Rashi says this indicates that Joseph was sold several times. First</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:549.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sold to the Ishmaelites who sold him to Midianites who then sold him to the Egyptians.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:567.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Bag opened in camp vs at home: One of the brothers opens his bag at the inn and discovers the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:581.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">money (It is inferred that this is Levi). Later back home the other brothers also find money</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:595.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in their own bags. Why didn’t all the brothers open their sacks? Double sided sacks, money at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:609.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the bottom of all sacks except that of Levi, who was most guilty for sale of Joseph. Evidently</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:623.86px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joseph wanted only one tranche of money to be discovered which would not have brought</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:637.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">them back to Egypt immediately professing innocence. Rather he wanted them to discover</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:651.94px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the money only after they reached home.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:673.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">7</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:5614px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background008.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:232.25px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canaan">Canaan</A> in the Late Bronze Age</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was a shadow of what it had been centuries earlier: many cities had been abandoned, others had</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shrunk in size, and the total settled population was probably not much more than a hundred</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thousand. Settlement was concentrated in cities along the coastal plain and along major trade routes.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The central and northern hill country which would later become the biblical kingdom of Israel was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">only sparsely inhabited, and </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem">Jerusalem</A> was a Canaanite city-state recognizing Egyptian suzerainty.</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Politically and culturally, Egypt was dominant; each Canaanite city had its own ruler, but was often</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">at odds with its neighbors, appealing to Egypt to adjudicate differences. The city-state system</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">broke down during the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse">Late Bronze Age,</A> and Canaanite culture was then gradually absorbed into</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that of the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philistines">Philistines, Phoenicians</A><span class="cls_003"> and Israelites. The process was gradual and a strong <A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt">Egyptian</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">presence continued into the 12th century BCE.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_022"><span class="cls_022">Archeological Periods in Canaan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Stone Age: c. 8500-4300 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:257.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Copper Age: 4300-3300 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:273.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Bronze Age: 3300-1200 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:289.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Early Bronze Age = 3300-2300 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:305.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Middle Bronze Age = 2300-1550 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:321.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Late Bronze Age = 1550-1200 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Iron Age: 1200-586 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian Period: 586-539 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:369.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Persian Period: 539-332 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hellenistic Period: 332-63 BC</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:401.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman Period: 63 BC-324 AD</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:182.78px;top:424.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Deconstructing the Walls of Jericho - Ze'ev Herzog</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:442.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This is what archaeologists have learned from their excavations in the Land of Israel: the Israelites</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:456.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">were never in Egypt, did not wander in the desert, did not conquer the land in a military campaign</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:470.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and did not pass it on to the 12 tribes of Israel. Perhaps even harder to swallow is the fact that the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:484.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">united monarchy of David and Solomon, which is described by the Bible as a regional power, was at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:499.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">most a small tribal kingdom. And it will come as an unpleasant shock to many that the God of Israel,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:513.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jehovah, had a female consort (Asherah) and that the early Israelite religion adopted monotheism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:527.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">only in the waning period of the monarchy and not at Mount Sinai. Most of those who are engaged</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:541.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in scientific work in the interlocking spheres of the Bible, archaeology and the history of the Jewish</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:555.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">people - and who once went into the field looking for proof to corroborate the Bible story - now</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:569.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">agree that the historic events relating to the stages of the Jewish people's emergence are radically</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:583.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">different from what that story tells.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:603.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">8</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:6416px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background009.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:259.01px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Myth of the Exodus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Even this foundational myth of the Jewish religion is riven with invention and inconsistencies:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:99.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">First of all, there is no evidence of any type that the Israelites were ever slaves in Egypt in the first</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:113.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">place. They may have been: a) members of a the Canaanite immigration in advance of the Hyksos</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invasion of Egypt  (around 1650 BC); b) even Hyksos themselves, since the Hyksos are suspected to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have been of Hurrian origin (Abraham’s birthplace). Indeed Josephus identifies the Exodus with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Manetho’s report of the emigration of 480,000 Hyksos “shepherd kings” from Egypt to Jerusalem</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(c 1550 BC). Apion even alleges that the heretic priest Osarseph changed his name to Moses and led</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a rebellion against Egypt. As archaeologist Jacquetta Hawkes states, “…they were wandering groups</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Semites who had long come to Egypt for trade and other peaceful purposes;” or c) perhaps they</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">were opportunistic members (habiru) of the coalition of the Sea Peoples (1200-900 BC), who</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">devastated the Mycenean world until stopped  (and enslaved?) by Egypt.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Second, there is no record of any sort outside of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">biblical scripture that describes the ten plagues</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">visited upon Egypt. This seems to be pure</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invention by Exilic scribes in Babylon.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Third, the passage of 603,550 armed men</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Numbers 1:46) with wives, children and “a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mixed multitude of non-Israelites” would have</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:341.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">formed a parade of nearly 2 million, who if</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:355.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">marching ten-abreast would form a column 150</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:369.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">miles long through the Sinai desert. Their place</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:383.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of habitation for 38 years after refusing to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:397.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">challenge the Canaanites, Kadesh Barnea, would</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have been the largest city in the Middle East, yet</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shows no signs at all of any habitation prior to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1000 BC.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:344.81px;top:442.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Egyptian Empire 1500-1200 BCE</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:458.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fourth, the culture of the earliest Israelite settlements is Canaanite, their cult objects are those of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:472.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Canaanite god El (before the adoption of the war god YHWH), the pottery remains are in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:486.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Canaanite tradition, and the alphabet used is early Canaanite. Almost the sole marker distinguishing</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:500.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the "Israelite" villages from Canaanite sites is an absence of pig bones.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:516.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fifth, Kings 6:1 maintains that the Exodus occurred 480 years before the construction of Solomon’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:530.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Temple: that would be 1450 BC. At that time, not only was Egypt not afraid of a foreign enemy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:544.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Pharaoh’s ostensible motive for suppressing the Israelites), but the Israelites would have been</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:558.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">escaping from Egypt to … Egypt! Canaan was part of the Egyptian empire (see map) until 1200 BC.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:574.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Finally, the widespread use of dromedaries (Exodus 9:3) was not known in Egypt until late in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:588.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">first millennium BC. Also, at the time of the “invasion” of Canaan by the Israelites, Jericho was not a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.58px;top:602.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">walled city at all, but was “small, poor, almost insignificant, and unfortified.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:622.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:303.29px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">9</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:7218px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background010.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:236.57px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joshua's “conquest” of Canaan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The returning Israelites are instructed by their “god” not to buy land as had Abraham, but rather to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invade and obliterate any remnant of the local culture.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:113.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Deut 7:2 “And when the Lord thy God shall deliver them before thee; thou shalt smite</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">them, and utterly destroy them; thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor shew mercy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto them:”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Perhaps the most unsettling part of the Exodus myth is that the Post-Exilic priests wrote the legends</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of early Israelite history in such a savage and chauvinistic tone. One case may serve as an exemplar:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:187.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Num 31:1 “And the LORD spake unto Moses, saying, </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-2/">2</A> Avenge the children of Israel of</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:201.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Midianites: afterward shalt thou be gathered unto thy people</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-3/">.3</A> And Moses spake unto</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the people, saying, Arm some of yourselves unto the war, and let them go against the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:229.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Midianites, and avenge the LORD of Midian…. </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-7/">7</A> And they warred against the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:243.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Midianites, as the LORD commanded Moses; and they slew all the males… </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-9/">9</A> And the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:257.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">children of Israel took all the women of Midian captives, and their little ones, and took the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:271.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spoil of all their cattle, and all their flocks, and all their goods. </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-10/">10</A> And they burnt all their</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:285.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cities  wherein they dwelt, and all their goodly castles, with fire. </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-11/">11</A> And they took all the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spoil, and all the prey, both of men and of beasts…</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:315.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-14/">14</A> And Moses was wroth with the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:329.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">officers of the host, with the captains</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:343.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">over thousands, and captains over</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hundreds, which came from the battle.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-15/">15</A> And Moses said unto them, Have ye</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">saved all the women alive? </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-16/">16</A> Behold,</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:399.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">these caused the children of Israel,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:413.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">through the counsel of Balaam, to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:427.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">commit trespass against the LORD in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:442.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the matter of Peor, and there was a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:456.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">plague among the congregation of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:156.50px;top:463.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“Thy will be done.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:470.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">LORD.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:486.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-17/">17</A> Now therefore kill every male among the little ones , and kill every woman that hath</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">known man by lying with him. </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-18/">18</A> But all the women children, that have not known a man</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by lying with him, keep alive for yourselves  …</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Numbers-31-35/">35</A> And thirty and two thousand persons in</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">all, of women that had not known man by lying with him… 47Even of the children of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:542.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Israel's half, Moses took one portion of fifty, both of man and of beast, and gave them unto</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:556.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Levites, which kept the charge of the tabernacle of the LORD; as the LORD</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:570.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">commanded Moses…</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">51And Moses and Eleazar the priest took the gold of them, even all wrought jewels  …53</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">For the men of war had taken spoil, every man for himself.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:616.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Later, in America, the Puritans would see themselves as latter-day Israelites coming into a new</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:630.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Canaan, where “God” (smallpox) had cleared the land before them. They thereupon acted as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joshua had and took over the settlements, killing men, women, and children without mercy.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:660.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Small wonder ‘patriotic American Christians’ were not upset with the killing of babies at My Lai.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:680.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">10</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:8020px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background011.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:251.81px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Human/Child Sacrifice</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:81.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">It seems the gods of Canaan and likewise YHWH had a taste for blood. Reference to sacrifices:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:95.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">By neighboring peoples to their gods: Burnt offerings of children are documented to Moloch (Deut</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:109.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">12:31, 2Kings 23:10), the sacrifice of the first-born by Moab (2Kings 3:27)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:123.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">By Israelites to YHWH: Josiah  burns human bones to YHWH (1Kings 13:1-2, 2Chron 34:1-5),</span></div>
