<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:137.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David sacrifices two of Saul’s sons and five of his grandsons to YHWH (2Sam 21:1, 8-14), a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:151.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">town and people are made a burnt offering to YHWH (Deut 13:13-19), YHWH kills all the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:165.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">first-born of Egypt (Ex 13:11-16), YHWH claims all the first-born of Israel as his (Ex 13:2),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:179.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH hands men over to be ‘fuel for the fire’ (Ez 21:33-37), YHWH demands Isaac be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:193.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sacrificed (Gen 22:2), a city-full of people is offered as a sacrifice to YHWH (Josh 6:21), a thief</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:207.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is burned to death (Josh 7:15), Jephthah sacrifices his daughter as a burnt offering to YHWH</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:221.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Judges 11:29-40), every devoted thing - both of man and beast - shall be put to death (Lev</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:235.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">27:28), Moses orders the murder of Midianite women and children (Num 31:25-40), YHWH</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:249.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gives statutes that the first-born are to ‘pass through the fire’ (Ez 20:25-26)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:263.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">By Israelites to other gods: Ahaz burns his son as an offering (2Kings 16:2-3), Manassah rebuilds</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:277.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">altars to Baal and worships foreign gods, as had Ahab (2Kings 21:1-6), Israelites sacrifice their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:291.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">children to Moloch (Ez 16:20-21, 23:37, Is 57:5, Jer 7:31, 19:5, 32:35, Lev 20:2, Ps 106:37-41)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:305.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Also note that in all of these legends, the only</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:319.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">important character is the male lead; the usually</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:333.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">nameless wives and children are mere ciphers:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:347.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Job’s original family, Lot’s wife, Lot’s daughter,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:361.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jephtha’s daughter, King Mesha’s son, Ahaz’s son,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:375.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Isaac, the Innocents. Human sacrifice is disguised</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:389.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as a necessity, blood sacrifice is preferred (hence</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:403.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">god’s preference for the offering of Abel), and of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:417.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">course, Jesus, whose sacrifice is memorialized by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:431.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a daily cannibalistic ritual. ‘Without the shedding of blood, there is no remission’ (Heb 9:13-22).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:445.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Indeed, the deaths of Job’s family are mere collateral damage of a wager between YHWH and Satan:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:460.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Job 1:12 </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-12/">And the LORD said unto Satan, Behold, all that he hath is in thy power; only upon</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:474.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-12/">himself put not forth thine hand. So Satan went forth from the presence of the LORD. 13 And</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:488.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-13/">there was a day when his sons and his daughters were eating and drinking wine in their eldest</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:502.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-13/">brother's house: 14 And there came a messenger unto Job, and said, The oxen were plowing, and</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:516.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-14/">the asses feeding beside them: 15 And the Sabeans fell upon them, and took them away; yea, they</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:530.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-15/">have slain the servants with the edge of the sword; and I only am escaped alone to tell thee. 16</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:544.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-16/">While he was yet speaking, there came also another, and said, The fire of God is fallen from</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:558.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-16/">heaven, and hath burned up the sheep, and the servants, and consumed them; and I only am</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-16/">escaped alone to tell thee. 17 While he was yet speaking, there came also another, and said, The</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-17/">Chaldeans made out three bands, and fell upon the camels, and have carried them away, yea, and</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-17/">slain the servants with the edge of the sword; and I only am escaped alone to tell thee. 18 While he</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:614.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-18/">was yet speaking, there came also another, and said, Thy sons and thy daughters were eating and</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:628.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-18/">drinking wine in their eldest brother's house: 19 And, behold, there came a great wind from the</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:642.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-19/">wilderness, and smote the four corners of the house, and it fell upon the young men, and they are</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:656.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Job-1-19/">dead; and I only am escaped alone to tell thee.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:676.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">11</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:8822px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background012.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:206.42px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">El, Baal, Asherah, and YHWH (Jehovah)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The earliest ancestor’s of Israel worshipped a god named El (Gen 16:13, 17:1, 21:33, 31:13, 35:7, 11,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">43:14, 58:3), El-Elohe-Israel (Gen 33:20), as well as the peace-loving god of vegetation in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Syro-Palestinian pantheon, Baal, and Asherah. The prevalence of their worship is evidenced by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the numerous times such altars must be removed. Their altars existed alongside those of YHWH</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as evidenced by Gideon’s father, Joash, who had altars to Baal and Asherah (Judges 6:25). The fact</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that Gideon had to destroy his father’s “pagan” altars at night, and was almost executed for his act,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">further indicates the widespread  acceptance of Baal and Asherah.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH was once viewed as a member of a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">pantheon ruled over by El.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Deut 32:8-9 When the most High (El)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">divided to the nations their inheritance, when</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he separated the sons of Adam, he set the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">bounds of the people according to the number</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the children of Israel. 9. For the LORD’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(YHWH’s) portion is his people: Jacob is the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">lot of his inheritance.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH seems to have achieved supremacy as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:323.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Israel’s national god due his military prowess</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:171.74px;top:329.33px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">Asherah</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(“YHWH of the Armies”), while in times of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">peace, Baal would ensure fertility. YHWH,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_god">national god</A> of war for both Israel and</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:379.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judah, seems to have originated in </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edom">Edom</A> and</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:393.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midian">Midian</A> in southern Canaan and may have been</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brought to Israel by the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenites">Kenites</A><span class="cls_003"> and <A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midianites">Midianites.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:421.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Worship of YHWH can be traced back to the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:436.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">time of Moses (Ex 6:3) and seems to be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:449.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">associated with the south of Palestine, for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:463.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Moses first encounters him in Midian (Ex 18).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:478.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Further Jael, a Kenite (southern) heroine in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:492.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH’s wars, is cited in Judg 5:24-30, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:506.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Deut 33:2</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">And he said, The LORD (YHWH)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">came from Sinai, and rose up from Seir</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:180.74px;top:546.67px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">Baal</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:548.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto them.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:564.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">With the emergence of the monarchy, the kings promoted their family god, </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahweh">Y</A><span class="cls_003">HWH, as the <A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henotheism">god of</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:578.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henotheism">the kingdom,</A> but beyond the royal court, religion continued to be polytheistic. The major deities</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:592.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">were not numerous - </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_%28god%29">El, Asherah</A><span class="cls_003"> (spouse of El?), YHWH, and <A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baal">Baal.</A> At an early stage El and</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:606.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH became fused and Asherah worship ceased as a separate state cult, although she continued</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:620.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to be popular at the local level until Persian times.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">12</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:9624px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background013.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:189.74px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Dubious Priestly Myth of David and Solomon</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">On editorial license and the legend of David: David raises the heretofore undistinguished</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Canaanite city of Jerusalem and the Judean Samuelite (Southern) priesthood to their positions</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of religious dominance, at the expense of Shiloh and the Elide (Northern) priesthood.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Solomon cultivates the priests, installing the line of Zadok as High Priests, and so Solomon’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sudden unlineal accession is justified at the expense of the legitimate heir, Adonijah.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Judean Zadokite priesthood (J) later edit</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and write the two main works of Israelite</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">history: Genesis to Second Kings (G2K) and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Chronicles (Chron), in which David is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">absolved of any knowledge of or guilt in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">deaths of his many enemies: Saul, Abner,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ishbosheth, and Absolom. Indeed, while G2K</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invents alibis for all David’s numerous</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">improprieties in his rise to power and reign:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that David was serving the Philistine</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">king Achish when Achish’s forces killed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saul;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and the irregularities of David’s reign:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:343.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">his alliance with Nahash, king of Ammon,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">enemy of Israel; extermination of Saul’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rightful successor, Ishbosheth, and the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rest of Saul’s line; Bathsheba; Absalom;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:399.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Sheba; Adonijah; and Solomon’s secret,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:341.21px;top:413.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sudden accession.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:429.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Chronicles simply ignores them. Chronicles overlaps with parts of G2K, but is a more</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:443.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">theologized (pro-Judean) version - stressing the role of Levites, virtually ignoring affairs of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:457.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the north (Israel), exaggerating numbers, replete with miraculous events, and giving a highly</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">idealized version of David. Legends unique to Chronicles must be approached with caution,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:486.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and are best viewed as a compendium of purposeful inventions from pro-Davidic Judean</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sources.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">13</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:10426px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background014.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:271.01px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Line of Saul</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a Benjamite representative of northern, Israelite interests, challenges the Philistines in the hill</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">country, rules Ephraim, and is supported by Elide priests of Shiloh, leading to conflict with Samuel.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saul is crowned king, offers sacrifice when Samuel is late and for that is blamed by Samuel. David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">comes to Saul’s court as a soldier, plays his flute for Saul, now portrayed as a solitary paranoiac, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">becomes his armor-bearer. David volunteers to Saul to kill Goliath and tries on Saul’s armor.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David kills the 9-foot tall Goliath. Samuel orders Saul to “kill all the Amelekites,” but Saul takes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Amelikite king Agog prisoner, whom Samuel kills. Samuel condemns Saul a second time for not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">killing Agog, and claims God has removed his blessing from Saul, so Samuel anoints David, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“the spirit of YHWH” (saving grace) is transferred from Saul to David. Saul’s son Jonathan loves</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David, and gives him his clothes (sign of abdication to David?). David’s fame as a military hero</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">exceeds that of Saul (1Sam18), so Saul is jealous of David. Saul’s daughter Michal marries David;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David flees to Samuel; Saul’s messengers sent to find David all begin prophesying; David flees to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Achish, the Philistine king of Gath, where he gathers a rebel army in the service of Achish, whose</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:265.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">forces kill Saul and Jonathan at Mount Gilboa, a battle from which David is suspiciously written out.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:279.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The people of Judah come to Hebron and anoint David, who rules Judah from Hebron for seven</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:293.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">years. He carries on good relations with the Philistines, and allies with Nahash, king of Ammon,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:307.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">enemy of Israel (1Sam11, 2Sam10, 17). A long war then ensues between David and the house of Saul</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:321.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(2Sam2)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:554.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1000 Ishbosheth is Saul’s rightful heir (and, unfortunately for him, a Northerner). Abner, Saul’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:568.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cousin, is the real power behind Ishbosheth. David is at this time allied with the Philistines. Abner</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:582.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">accesses Saul’s harem as the first step to taking power, is chastised, begins negotiations with David,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:596.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">comes to David at Hebron, seals the agreement betraying Ishbosheth, and is then and there</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:610.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">assassinated by David’s military commander, Joab (David is aghast!) ; then Ishbosheth is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:624.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">assassinated (David is unconsolable!).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:644.98px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">14</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:11228px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background015.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:235.49px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1Chronicles - All About Dave</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:81.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">From Adam to Israel - a genealogical list, arranged with Israel last and pointing to its election by God.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:95.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Tribes of Israel - Emphasis on Judah, Benjamin, and Levi: the “loyal” tribes in the schism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:109.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jabez's Prayer preaches the  “Health-Wealth Gospel,” ignoring care for others and faithful service.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:123.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Restored Jerusalem Community  - the crucial link between Chron's community and their past.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:137.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saul as an example of unfaithfulness: Chron is only interested in the death of Saul, who is a foil for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:151.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David and Solomon, as alterations in the source material make clear.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:165.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David as King of All Israel: the lurid aspects in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:179.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Samuel are largely ignored: the war between</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:193.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saul and David, his adultery with Bathsheba,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:207.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">his murder of Uriah, the questionable</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:221.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">circumstances of Solomon's birth, and the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:235.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">struggle for power between David's sons .</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:249.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David First Brings the Ark to Jerusalem to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:263.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">establish proper worship, at odds with 2Sam5-6,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:277.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">where David first defeats the Philistines and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:291.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">then rebuilds Jerusalem. After Uzzah's death</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:305.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for touching the ark, David orders that only</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:319.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Levites carry the ark, ascribing a liturgical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:333.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">practice from Chron’s own day to David’s.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:347.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">God’s Promises that David’s line will always be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:361.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">on the throne of Judah and that of forgiveness</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:375.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to Solomon form the two pillars of the theology</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:389.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the returning exiles.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:366.91px;top:388.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David notices Bathsheba</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:403.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David’s Wars are successful when he trusts God. The Ammonite War is omitted, possibly because</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:417.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of David's adultery with Bathsheba, his murder of her husband, and implied illegitimacy of their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:431.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">progeny, Solomon.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:445.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David’s Census at the urging of “Satan” (1Chron 21:1) displeases God and results in severe plagues.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:460.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">So who is "Satan" and why does he incite David? The Hebrew word satan means adversary. In Job</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:474.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and Zechariah, it implies a divine being, though not yet the dualistic personification of Evil of later</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:488.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judaism and the New Testament, a concept that emerges during the Persian era. It seems best to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:502.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">interpret David's Satan as "a human adversary," perhaps a military threat. But then 2Sam24:1 states,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:516.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“Again the anger of the LORD was kindled against Israel, and he incited David against them,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:530.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">saying, 'Go, count the people of Israel and Judah'" Is God’s anger Satan? And what's so wrong with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:544.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">counting the people, anyway? Is it because apportioning Israel for taxation and conscription was a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:558.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">drastic change from long-held beliefs in Israel's tradition, or did David's numbering of the people</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">arise from prideful assumptions about military might that led him away from trust in God?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David has "shed much blood." And so  commissions Solomon as the divinely chosen temple builder.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David authorizes a Temple bureaucracy that only existed in the postexilic period.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:614.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David Transfers the Kingdom and Charges Solomon (totally at odds with 1K1-2). There is no</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:628.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">controversy over who will be king, no mention of Nathan, Bathsheba, or Adonijah. Solomon has</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:642.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">no one killed and does not engage in the palace intrigues that occupy the initial chapters of 1 Kings.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:656.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The repeated notice is only that God has chosen Solomon to rule Israel and build the temple.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:676.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">15</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:12030px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background016.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.57px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">King David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1000 BCE With the murder of Ishbosheth, the path is finally clear for David and his Judean priest</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zadok to take over. The elders of Israel come to David and anoint him. David conquers Jerusalem,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">up to that time a very modest settlement whose name means “founded by Shalem (a Canaanite</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">god)”, and brings the ark of the covenant to Jerusalem (to the resentment of the ten Northern</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">tribes). Nathan pronounces YHWH’s blessing on David’s kingship and promises his dynasty will</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">last forever (2Sam7). David executes Saul’s descendants (2Sam21) and empowers the High Priest</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zadok and Levites from Bethlehem, loyal to David, who are scattered throughout the kingdom, a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">priesthood, not unlike the Jesuits, fiercely loyal to their king. David fights frontier wars with the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Philistines, Moabites, Edomites, Ammonites, and Aramaeans. "Zion theology," the idea that the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">god of Israel has chosen Jerusalem for his dwelling-place and that the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davidic_dynasty">Davidic dynasty</A> will reign</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">there forever, becomes the state ideology. The House of David rules Jerusalem for four hundred</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">years to 586 BCE. G2K makes an obvious effort to present David in a favorable light, as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">YHWH’s Chosen One. “House of David” appears in the Tell Dan inscription.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:627.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David as the Psalmist? - ledawid, the term based on which the Psalms are attribute to David, likely</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:641.14px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">means not “by David,” but rather dedicated “to David.” David is portrayed chiefly as a musician in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:655.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Chronicles, though G2K has little on this aspect. The later the version of the story, the more psalms</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:669.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">are ascribed to David.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:685.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">16</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:12832px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background017.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:226.01px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Absolom, Adonijah, and Solomon</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0970 BCE The most senior and noble of David’s remaining sons (son of an Aramaean princess from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Geshur 2Sam3:3, the only one of David’s sons of royal blood, since Amnon had been killed by him</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for raping their sister Tamar), Absolom enjoys popular support, rises against David, and David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">flees Jerusalem, but not before installing his ally Hushai as a disinformant “adviser” to Absalom.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Absalom takes over David’s harem (now there’s no turning back). David deploys Ittai and 600</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Philistine mercenaries (2Sam15). Hushai discredits Achitophel; Absalom is defeated at Gilead, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is killed by Joab, whom David executes for not dealing “gently” with Absalom. David is restored,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">then executes all of Saul’s male descendants. The next in line of David’s sons, Adonijah, proclaims</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">himself king (1Kings 1:5-8). Nathan reports Adonijah’s actions to Bathsheba, who convinces the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">senile David to authorize the crowning of her son, Solomon, in a surprise ceremony orchestrated</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by Nathan, Zadok and Benaiah (1Kings 1:38-40).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0967-0928 BCE Solomon - Legends are written</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">into Scripture of the Queen of Sheba and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Solomon’s reign as a “golden age,” stretching</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from the Euphrates (?!) to the Egyptian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">frontier. Solomon is reputed to be wealthy,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">powerful, and wise.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">But is he “wealthy”? Cash flow problems force</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">him to sell twenty cities in Galilee to the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Phoenician king of Tyre (1Kings 9:10), and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">there are no trade items in Solomonic ruins.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:383.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Is he “powerful”? He is constantly troubled by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:397.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hadad of Edom, Rezin of Damascus, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jeroboam of Ephraim (1Kings 11:10), his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:427.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">adversaries sent by YHWH “because his wives</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:442.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">had turned Solomon’s heart to other gods”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:102.38px;top:455.83px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Uxorious Solomon worships a foreign god</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:455.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(priestly self-justification).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:469.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Is he “wise”? He used forced labor and other despotic practices that caused the kingdom to break into</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:484.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">two immediately after his death (1Kings 12:1). Furthermore, he is not mentioned in any non-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:498.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judean sources. Religiously, Solomon had broken the mandate of the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torah">Torah</A> by marrying foreign</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:512.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wives, and worshipping and building shrines to the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moab">Moabite</A><span class="cls_003"> and <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ammon">Ammonite</A> gods (1Kings 11:1-13).</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Why then is he so represented? Again, it is because he is credited with building the Temple and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:540.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">establishing the Zadokite sacerdotal ascendancy, so he is a hero to the priests, who later edited and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wrote the Scriptures. He succeeds David as king, and forms diplomatic alliances through marriage.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:568.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He builds the First Temple on Mt. Moriah, which becomes the only acceptable location for sacrifice,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:582.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thereby granting a religious monopoly to the Zadokites. Chronicles ignores the issue of Solomon’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:596.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">accession by having David designate him as his successor, and omits all unseemly circumstances,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:610.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">such as the attacks by Hiram of Tyre, Hadad, Rezin, Jeroboam, forced labor, and Ahijah’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:624.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prediction that Jeroboam would rule.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:704.98px" class="cls_002"><span class="cls_002">17</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:13634px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background018.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:193.46px;top:67.32px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Solomon’s successor? The Zadokite Priesthood!</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:85.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0928 BCE Solomon dies, and simmering conflicts split the country between the northern Ten</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:99.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Tribes: Reuben, Dan, Naphtali, Gad, Asher, Issachar, Zebulun, Joseph (split into Ephraim,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:113.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Manasseh, and Machir [Manasseh east of the Jordan] ) and the four southern tribes: Judah, Levi</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(divested of land), Simeon (surrounded and assimilated by Judah), and Benjamin (conquered by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judah in 955). The most divisive issue between Israel (the northern ten) and Judah (the southern</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">four) is the requirement that sacrifice to YHWH be performed exclusively by Zadokite priests at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Temple in Jerusalem. This policy effectively delists Shiloh, the location of the Tent of Meeting</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Joshua 18:1), where the Ark of the Covenant had been kept, defrocks its Aaronite priesthood, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:197.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">constitutes a declaration of religious war.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:218.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Hebrew Scriptures will be written by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:232.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">southern Judean scribes, who demand exclusive</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:246.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Yahwism (no gods but YHWH), and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:260.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">condemn Israel. Jeroboam, the Ephraimite head</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:274.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Solomon’s forced labor operations, is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:288.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">proclaimed by Ahijah of Shiloh as YHWH’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:302.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“next man” (1Kings 11:29), who will become</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:316.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">king of the northern tribes; he flees to Egypt</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:331.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">until Solomon’s death.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:346.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">At Solomon’s death, the Assembly at Shechem is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:361.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">convened to crown Rehoboam. Leaders of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:375.05px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ten northern tribes ask Rehoboam if he intends</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:389.09px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to be as repressive as Solomon; Rehoboam</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:403.13px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">responds that he will be worse:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:419.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“My father made your yoke heavy, but I will</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:433.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">add to your yoke: my father also chastised you</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:447.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with whips, but I will chastise you with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:461.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">scorpions." (1Kings 12:14).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:479.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The split is justified by the Judean editors of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:493.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Scripture as punishment for Solomon’s failure</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:507.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to follow priestly exhortations; namely by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:521.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">marrying foreign wives and worshipping</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:535.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">foreign gods. (1Kings 11:9-12):</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:553.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“9. And the LORD was angry with Solomon,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:567.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">because his heart was turned from the Lord</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:581.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">God of Israel ... 10 And had commanded him</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:599.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">That he should not go after other gods…11.Wherefore the LORD said unto Solomon,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:613.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Forasmuch as this is done of thee, and thou hast not kept my covenant and my statutes, which I</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:627.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have commanded thee, I will surely rend the kingdom away from thee and will give it to thy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:641.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">servant. 12 Notwithstanding in thy days, I will not do it for David thy father’s sake: but I will</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:655.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rend it out of the hand of thy son."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:299.93px;top:671.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
