<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:474.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rings, and the ornaments for the right hand, (six items)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:261.77px;top:491.59px" class="cls_013"><span class="cls_013">םיטירחהו תˣחפט˙הו תˣפטע˙הו תˣצלח˙ה</span><span class="cls_012">  </span><span class="cls_014">בכ</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:513.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-3-22/">22</A> The changeable suits of apparel, and the mantles, and the wimples, and the crisping pins,(four items)</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:531.19px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">22 καὶ τὰ ἐπιβλήματα τὰ κατὰ τὴν οἰκίαν καὶ τὰ διαφανῆ Λακωνικὰ</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:541.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">22 and the garments with purple grounds, and the shawls to be worn in the house, and the Spartan transparent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:555.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">dresses, (three items)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:286.61px;top:572.83px" class="cls_013"><span class="cls_013">םידידרהו תˣפינצהו םינידסהו םינילגהו</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:550.90px;top:572.83px" class="cls_014"><span class="cls_014">גכ</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:594.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-3-23/">23</A> The mirrors, and the fine linen, and the hoods, and the veils. (four items)</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:612.34px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">23  καὶ  τὰ  βύσσινα  καὶ  τὰ  ὑακίνθινα  καὶ  τὰ  κόκκινα  καὶ  τὴν  βύσσον,  σὺν  χρυσῷ  καὶ  ὑακίνθῳ</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:626.14px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">συγκαθυφασμένα καὶ θέριστρα κατάκλιτα.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:636.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">23 and those made of fine linen, and the purple [ones], and the scarlet [ones], and the fine linen, interwoven with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:650.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gold and purple, and the light coverings for couches. (six items)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:286.61px;top:670.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">30</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:24060px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background031.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:219.65px;top:35.16px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Emergence of Messianic Apocalyticism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:55.32px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0200 Messianism independent of Apocalypticism emerges. The Machabees avoid references to Messianism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:69.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">because they are not Davidic, but were usurpers. Messianism is intended to be restorative, directed inward, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in accord with natural laws. Sometimes theory has two Messiahs: a king and a priest, Moses and Aaron.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:97.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Apocalypticism is, on the other hand, utopian, eschatological, directed outward, supernatural, not necessarily</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:111.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Messianic; the Messiah would gather the banished Is 11:12.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:259.49px;top:312.77px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Participatory Messianism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:326.09px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0198 Antiochus III (Seleucid) takes Jerusalem after a siege, then allows the Jews to remain largely self-governing.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:340.13px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ethics are to be governed by ancestral laws; Jewish elites align with the foreign occupiers (again).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:356.09px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0189 The Seleucids are defeated by Rome at Magnesia. Yet another foreign invader is at the door.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:372.17px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0187-0175 Seleucus IV succeeds Antiochus, and loots the Jerusalem temple to pay reparations to Rome. Good</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:386.21px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">relations with the Jewish aristocracy are harmed. Hellenization is widespread among the upper classes, as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:400.25px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">indicated by the prevalence of Greek names. Religious and social conservatives conflict with Hellenizers.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:416.21px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0186 In order to unite his ruled territories, Antiochus III imposes paganism on the Jews.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:432.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0180 Joshuah Ben Sirach cites the Torah and Prophets as the Jewish canon to which, once definitively established,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:446.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">no new works can be added.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:462.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0176 The Heliodorus Affair - High Priest Onius III is accused by a certain Simon of under-reporting tax income</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:476.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to the Seleucids; Heliodorus is sent by Antiochus III to Jerusalem and conducts an audit; Onius III goes to the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:490.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Seleucid capital of Antioch to make his case; Antiochus III is assassinated; Antiochus IV takes over.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:506.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0175 Antiochus IV Epiphanes. The position of Jewish High Priest is bought by a certain Jason, who then</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:520.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hellenizes Jerusalem and renames the city Antioch in honor of Antiochus IV.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:536.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0172 High Priest Jason is replaced by Menelaus, a far more radical Hellenizer, who seeks to bring Jews into the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:550.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mainstream of Greek social and political life.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:566.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0168 Antiochus invades Egypt to achieve his dream of a united Hellenist East. At the gates of Alexandria he is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:580.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ordered to withdraw by the Roman ambassador, Gaius Popillius Laenas. Antiochus says he must think about it,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:594.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">upon which Laenas draws a line in the sand around Antiochus and replies, “You’ll think about it here!” Antiochus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:608.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">withdraws and rumors are spread that he has died. Conservatives in Jerusalem depose Menelaus and undo the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:622.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hellenizing reforms. Antiochus isn’t dead, suppresses the revolt brutally, brings a Greek garrison into Jerusalem,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:636.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">introduces pagan rites into the Temple, and outlaws Jewish customs. Jewish martyrs arise: Mattathias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:650.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Hasmonean) refuses to worship the Greek gods, and sparks a revolt in Jerusalem. His son, Judah Machabee (the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:664.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hammer) leads a guerrilla war against the Seleucids.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:680.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:302.09px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">31</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:24862px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background032.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:269.45px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Machabees</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0167 Judah Machabee besieges the Greek garrison in Jerusalem</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:63.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0167 The Book of Daniel is composed and written back into the days of the Babylonian captivity. Continued</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:77.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">domination by a parade of foreign powers in spite of the piety of the priests and people discredits the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:91.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Deuteronomist view and heralds the emergence of Apocalypticism. The characteristics of apocalyptic works are:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:105.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">pseudonymity - visions are attributed to figures from the past; numerical symbolism; secret language -</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:119.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">contemporary rulers referred to by past rulers; animal symbolism; doctrine of angels; division of history into</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:133.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">periods (of which the Greek is the fourth and final); references to the coming time; and belief in one or more</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:147.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Messiahs who would deliver Israel from foreign domination (a point conveniently overlooked by Christians).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:163.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0164 The Machabean rebels are victorious. Jonathan Machabee becomes High Priest, though he is not a Zadokite,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:177.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and purifies the Temple - the origin of Hanukkah. The Zadokites then evolve into 1) the Egyptian Leontopolis</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:191.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cult under Onius IV, 2) Jerusalem’s Sadducees, and 3) the Essenes of the Qumran sect. Some see this period also</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:205.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as a civil war between orthodox and </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_Judaism">Hellenized Jews.</A> Hasmonean kings attempt to revive the Judah described in</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:219.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Bible: a Jewish monarchy ruling from Jerusalem over all territories once ruled by David and Solomon. In</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:233.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">order to carry out this project, the </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean">Hasmoneans</A> forcibly convert Moabites, Edomites, and Ammonites, as well as</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:247.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the lost kingdom of Israel (Samaritans) to Judaism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:214.97px;top:445.15px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Antiochus seeks to eradicate the Jewish Religion</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:458.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0161 Judah Machabee renews the treaty with Rome to weaken Hellenism; Jews assert their nationalism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:474.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0150 Testaments of the Patriarchs - a text is written of ‘the speeches that should have been made.’ Levi and Judah are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:488.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">associated as dual Messiah figures.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:504.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0150 Jubilees - a text retelling stories within a framework of seven years, with the use of a solar calendar, written in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:518.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ethiopic, containing many historical anachronisms and talking animals.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:534.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0142 The Seleucids free Hasmonean Judea from paying taxes to the Empire. The Machabees are recognized as a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:548.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">new dynasty “until a new prophet shall arise,” … or the Romans (63 BCE).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:564.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0134-0104 John Horchanus I succeeds his father Simon Machabee. Besieged in Jerusalem by the Seleucid Antiochus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:578.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">VII, he first removes, then readmits non-combatants. The walls of Jerusalem are broken down. After the death</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:592.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Antiochus VII, the Seleucid Empire begins to break up. Horchanus robs the Tomb of David to support a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:606.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mercenary army, by which he expands his kingdom (Idumea), destroys the (schismatic) Samaritan temple (111</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:620.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">BCE), and forces conversions of non-Jewish populations, among whom is the grandfather of Herod the Great.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:636.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0130 1 Machabees in Hebrew relates Jewish history 175-135 BCE. Mattathias, like Phineas in Numbers, gives</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:650.86px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">legitimacy to Hasmoneans.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:666.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0120 2 Machabees in Greek relates the ideology of martyrdom, resurrection, Judaism, Hellenism, and how Jews</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:680.86px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">can live in the diaspora.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:696.94px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.37px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">32</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:25664px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background033.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:215.33px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Essenes: (the Dead Sea Scroll sect?)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0120 believe that all is decided by fate (no free will). They separate themselves from the vulgar, impure priesthood</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:61.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and people, and bear many similarities to Christians: baptism, contemporizing prophecies, solar calendar,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:75.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">communal organization, Messianic vocabulary, apocalypticism, predestination, and dualism. They avoid the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:89.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">corrupt city and expect a Davidic Messiah and a future world (Daniel) in which the Davidic monarchy is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:103.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">guaranteed forever (Is 11:6, Jeremiah 23, Zechariah).  Then God’s wrath will cease and He will establish a new</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:117.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">covenant with them alone. The Dead Sea Scrolls: The War Scroll - in a final battle, setbacks are to be expected, but</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:131.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">God’s intervention will be decisive. Pesher are texts with contemporary interpolation of prophecies. The sect</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:145.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">goes extinct after the Fall of Jerusalem (70 CE).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:326.33px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0104-0103 Aristobolus I conquers Galilee, forces conversion to Judaism of Galileans.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:342.29px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0103-0076 Alexander Jannaeus (Greek name) defeats a rebellion, banquets as the rebels’ wives and children of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:356.33px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rebels are killed in front of the crucified rebels. The Hasmoneans have themselves become thoroughly Hellenized.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:372.41px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0076 Salome Alexandra, wife of Alexander, becomes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:386.33px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">regent and empowers the Pharisees against the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:400.37px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saducees, whom she removes from Jerusalem.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:416.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0067 Hasmonean Civil War: Alexandra dies and her</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:430.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">two sons Hyrcanus II and Aristobolus II both seek</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:444.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman help. The two trade titles as the Romans</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:458.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">solidify their rule over Judea.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:474.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0066 Rebellion: Cataclysm is imminent: should zealots</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:488.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">themselves light the fuse (Pharisees) or will all happen</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:502.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">according to the Divine Plan (Sadducees)? Ethnic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:516.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and social tensions erupt (some burn debt records);</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:530.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Rome aids its allies, the aristocrats. After initial</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:544.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">successes for the rebels, Vespasian isolates Jerusalem.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:558.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Yohanan ben Zakkai escapes in a coffin, meets</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:572.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Vespasian, predicts his kingship. Vespasian is pleased,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:586.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and asks what ben Zakkai wants, to which he replies</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:600.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“Give me only Yavne (anachronistic, the town was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:614.86px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not yet built) and its wise men (not the priests?!).”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:628.90px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ben Zakkai establishes the first synagogue in Judea,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:118.82px;top:634.54px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Mattathias Slays an Idolater</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:642.94px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">citing Moses as the first rabbi.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:658.90px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.85px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">33</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:26466px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background034.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:270.65px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman Period</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0063 The Roman general Pompey conquers this last nominally independent kingdom of </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea">Judea.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:63.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0048 Pompey is defeated by Julius Caesar in 48, and Antipater of Edom becomes the first Roman Procurator.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:79.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0045 Jews refuse to assimilate. Jewish law tries to separate Jews from gentiles to prevent Jews from adopting</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:93.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">idolatrous behaviors. In Jewish law, a gentile is grouped together with dishonest butchers, gamblers, usurers and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:107.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thieves who cannot act as witnesses; and charity from non-Jews is not to be accepted. Dietary laws also limit social</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:121.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">interactions; e.g., food cooked by non-Jews is prohibited; hence, Shakespeare’s Shylock: “I will not eat with you.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:137.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0044 Caesar is assassinated and Quintus Labienus, Roman general and ambassador to the Parthians (Persians),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:151.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sides with the Liberators (Caesar’s assassins), and assists the Parthians in invading Roman territories.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0040 Parthians overrun Syria and Palestine and empower Antigonus. Herod (son of Antipater) goes to Rome,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">befriends Marc Antony, and is declared King of the Jews by the Roman Senate.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:197.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0037 Herod the Great expels the Parthians, retakes Judea, eliminates the Hasmoneans, and installs a Babylonian as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:211.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">High Priest. Alexandra, the mother of his Hasmonean wife Mariomne, is upset, so she contacts Cleopatra VII to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:225.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have Marc Antony appoint her son, Aristobulus III, as High Priest. He is appointed, and is enthusiastically</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:239.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">supported by the people, but Herod feels threatened, and so kills Aristobulus.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0031 The Battle of Actium. Octavian defeats Marc Antony and Cleopatra VII; Herod meets with Octavian,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">convinces Octavian to keep him as king, and executes a brutal repression. He kills his beloved wife Meriomne, her</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:283.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mother Alexandra, and Meriomne’s Hasmonean sons. This, or the example of Alexander Jannaeus, is likely the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:297.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inspiration for the tale of the Holy Innocents. Herod further fills Jerusalem with Hellenistic architecture, expands</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:311.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Temple, and brings in diaspora priests.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:249.77px;top:510.19px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Herod greets the Three Kings</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:521.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0004 BCE Herod the Great dies, leaving three sons, all named Herod: 1) Herod Archelaus succeeds his father as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:535.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ruler in Judea, Idumea, and Samaria. 2) Herod Philip rules Golan, marries Herodias, lives until 34; 3) Herod</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:549.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Antipas rules in Galilee and Parea until 39, marries Herodias (his late brother Philip’s widow), and executes John</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:563.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Baptist. Jesus is born.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:577.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Common Era (AD)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:593.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0006 Herod Archelaus is judged incompetent and is removed as the last </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnarch">ethnarch.</A>  ; a Roman prefect (later</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:607.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Pontius Pilate) is brought in. Quirinius, Governor of Syria, assesses property for taxation purposes (the ‘census’ in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:621.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Luke). The territories of Judea are combined with those of </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Idumea">Idumea</A><span class="cls_003"> and <A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samaria">Samaria</A> and governed as Judaea Province</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:635.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">under direct </span><A HREF="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_empire">Roman</A> administration. The government is moved to Caesarea Maritima, which has better</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:649.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">communications. Organized resistance to Rome begins: Judah of Gamila and Zadok the Pharisee (proponent of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:663.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Fourth Philosophy) preach that ‘subservience to Rome is idolatry.’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:679.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.29px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">34</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:27268px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background035.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:272.81px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">John and Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0025 John the Baptist, an Apocalyptic preacher, feeds the hopes of Apocalyptic Jews who are expecting a human</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:61.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Messiah descended from David to rule over an independent restored kingdom of Israel.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:77.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0029 Herod Antipas marries Herodias (who had</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:91.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">divorced his brother Philip), and executes John the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:105.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Baptist, either because he objected to Antipas’ marriage</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:119.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to Herodias, or because John was an eloquent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:133.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">revolutionary, fond of quoting Is 40:3 “prepare the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:147.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">way.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:163.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0030 Ministry of Jesus - (See Part Two for a discussion</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:177.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the criteria used to ferret out the “Historical Jesus.”)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:191.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus is born in Nazareth (a backward village so</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:205.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">insignificant it is not mentioned once in the Hebrew</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:219.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Scriptures or Josephus) to Mary and Joseph (Joseph is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:233.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">never heard from again) around 4 BC, and had</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:247.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">siblings - both brothers (James et al), and sisters (Mk</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:261.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3:31). He is born and raised as a Jew, in an area of Galilee</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:275.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that had been forcibly converted to Judaism by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:289.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Aristobolus I in 104 BCE.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:305.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus was most probably trained to be a tekton - carpenter,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:319.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">or construction worker of some sort, and seems to have</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:333.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">been drawn to the apocalyptic teaching of his “cousin”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:347.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Luke 1:36), John the Baptist. Beginning with his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:361.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">baptism by John, Jesus taught an Apocalyptic message.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:377.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In Matthew, Jesus’ first recorded preaching (4:17 Repent: for the kingdom of heaven is at hand.) is a direct quote</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:391.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from John and Jesus seems to have been guided into thinking of himself as the Messiah by his desire to fulfill John’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:406.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">expectations.He began his ministry in his native Galilee, but was not well received either by his family (Mk 3:21,31,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:420.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">John 7:5, Paul 1Cor 15) or the neighboring towns of Galilee (Mk 6:1, Lk 4, L 10, M 11). Though the chief Galilean</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:433.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cities of Cepherus and Tiberius were within walking distance, Jesus is never recorded as having gone there. He is a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:448.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophet without honor (Mk, John, Thomas), who had no home (Mk 8, Lk 9, John 15:18). Much in the mold of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:462.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Isaiah, he shares John’s contempt for the Pharisees (Jews who emphasize minute adherence to the letter rather than</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:476.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the spirit of the Law) and Sadducees (“smug” priests of the Temple in Jerusalem and collaborators with Rome),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:490.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and is concerned for the long-suffering multitudes.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:506.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He goes to Jerusalem at Passover apparently to cement his reputation as a prophet and to make his theological points,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">perhaps even to incite an armed uprising. He overturns the tables of money-changers and, as intended, attracts the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unfavorable attention of the Jewish authorities by disrupting Temple activities and preaching the imminent arrival</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:548.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the apocalyptic Kingdom of Heaven.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:564.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He is betrayed by his disciple Judas, who likely tells the Roman authorities that Jesus is claiming to be the Messiah and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:578.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">future ruler of Palestine. He is arrested (while with his band of armed “zealots”), tried by Pontius Pilate, crucified,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:592.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and probably dies on the cross, though Josephus tells of two men who survived crucifixion. Details of his death are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:606.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inconsistent (see notes below on Matthew 28). As for his “resurrection,” he is most likely buried in a mass grave, as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:620.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was the usual Roman custom for those guilty of treason.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:636.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.49px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">35</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:28070px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background036.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:272.21px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus’ Teachings</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">are best summarized by the Sermon on the Mount with the Beatitudes and Antitheses:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:63.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus on love: ‘Love your neighbor as yourself,’ a sentiment already present in Leviticus. Also, in stark contrast to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:77.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Nahum 1:2 ‘The lord takes vengeance on his adversaries (Gentiles) and rages against his enemies,’ and the beliefs</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:91.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the Qumran sect that one should love certain people (our sect), hate everyone else (even Jews), Jesus proposes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:105.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">loving one’s enemies.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:362.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus also broke with convention by consciously associating with women and repentant sinners rather than with the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:376.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">proudly self-righteous; he preferred the attitude of sinful humility to that of smug spiritual superiority.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:392.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Regarding salvation, Matthew 25, discussed in greater detail below, is Jesus’ clearest doctrinal pronouncement.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:406.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">With its unambiguous endorsement of “works,” it directly contradicts later Pauline emphasis on “faith.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:422.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus was doubtless an Apocalypticist. The earliest sources - Q, Mark, M, Lk, and Paul - are all apocalyptic (cf,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:436.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1Enoch 69, Dan 7:13ff, Paul 1Cor 15:23, 1Thess 4:16ff, Mk 1:15, 8:38, 9:1!, 13:24ff, 13:30!, 14:62, Matthew 25:13;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:450.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">19:28! (twelve thrones), Luke 17:24, 12:40). Apocalypticism was a widespread philosophical school in 1</span><span class="cls_010">st</span><span class="cls_003"> century</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:464.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Palestine, which asserted that: the world is clearly divided between the powers of good and evil, that they then</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:478.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">lived in an age of evil, that nothing can save the world except the direct intervention of God, that God’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:492.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">intervention is imminent (Mk 9:1), that the beginning of God’s intervention will be signaled by resurrection of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:506.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the good who suffered and the evil who inflicted suffering to face judgment. After it becomes evident that the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:520.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Coming is not imminent, the message is changed: Mark 9:1 was toned down to Lk17:20. Then John 11:23</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:534.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">modifies it even further, saying that resurrection occurs whenever one had faith.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:550.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">36</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:28872px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background037.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:241.61px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Reaction to the Crucifixion</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:47.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0033 After Jesus' sudden and shocking death, his followers spread his message and embellish or invent stories of his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:61.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">life. Our challenge is to separate the aspects of this remarkable life which are more likely to be historical from those</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:75.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that are not. Especially suspect are stories that feature angels, dreams, miracles, predictions of the future, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:89.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">fulfillment of prophecies. Sometimes actual stories are embellished with miraculous features. Healing the sick and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:103.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">raising the dead may be examples of this. It is possible that people experienced a placebo effect merely from the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:117.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">touch of the holy man, similar to the effect of the Elder Zossima in Brothers Karamazov or the effect of Caesar's</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:131.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">presence upon his soldiers as described in Decline and Fall of the Roman Empire. It is also possible that Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:145.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mastered some of the magical tricks of the prophetic trade and impressed the mobs as can Penn and Teller. It is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:159.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">important to note that magic was a staple of the period and even Simon Magus was seen flying in the book of Acts.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:173.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">It is likewise no wonder that believers whose fundamental faith is based upon a miracle (the Resurrection) should</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:187.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have no qualms about mythologizing the life of their leader. After his death, convinced, in spite of overwhelming</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:201.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">evidence to the contrary, that Jesus was the Messiah, believers pored over the Jewish Scriptures searching for any</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophecy regarding the Messiah and write the fulfillment of those prophecies back into the life of Jesus, changing</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:229.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">details wherever instructed by the "Holy Spirit."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:245.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">As for Jesus’ elevation to the status as God, the early Christian community believe that he was deified upon his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:259.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">resurrection as attested by Pre-literary Traditions (terse statements in tightly structured formats with parallel</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:273.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">statements).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:289.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">One such fragment appears in Paul:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:305.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Romans 1</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Romans-1-3/">:3</A> Concerning his Son Jesus Christ our</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:319.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Lord, which was made of the seed of David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:333.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">according to the flesh; </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Romans-1-4/">4</A> And declared to be the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:347.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Son of God with power, according to the spirit</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:361.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of holiness, by the resurrection from the dead:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:377.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul was planning a mission to Spain and required the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:391.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">help of the Christian community in Rome. Here he is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:406.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">trying to show that he is of one spirit with them by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:420.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">appealing to an earlier statement of faith, using</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:434.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">phrases not characteristic of Paul (‘seed of David,’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:448.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">‘spirit of holiness,’ and not reflective of his beliefs</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:462.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Jesus becoming the son of God at Resurrection).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:478.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Two more appear in Acts:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:494.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Acts 2:36 Peter: Therefore let all the house of Israel know assuredly, that God hath made the same Jesus,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:508.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">whom ye have crucified, both Lord and Christ.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:524.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Acts 13:33 Paul: God hath fulfilled the same unto us their children, in that he hath raised up Jesus again; as it is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:63.00px;top:538.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">also written in the second Psalm, Thou art my Son, this day have I begotten thee.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Acts (written 80-85 AD) furthermore cannot be a record of the actual speeches, as Peter, an illiterate Aramaic-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:568.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">speaker, sounds just like Paul, an educated Greek-speaker.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:584.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">For the evangelist Mark, Jesus was adopted by God at his baptism. Such adoption was common in the Roman</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:598.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">world (cf, Octavian). As the community develops and the gospels are written, the divinization of Jesus is pushed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:612.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">further and further back: from the resurrection for the pre-literary tradition, to baptism for Mark, to his birth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:626.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for Matthew and Luke, and finally to the moment of creation for John.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:642.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.01px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">37</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:29674px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background038.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:208.37px;top:30.72px" class="cls_015"><span class="cls_015">Jesus and James vs Paul and Augustine</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:49.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">What is Jesus’ teaching regarding salvation?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:63.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus here gives a clear protocol for salvation; namely, to help those in need, even anonymously.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:350.23px;top:77.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Matthew 25 - Parable of the Sheep and Goats</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:324.05px;top:91.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 25:31 When the Son of man shall come in his glory,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:105.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and all the holy angels with him, then shall he sit upon</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:119.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the throne of his glory: 25:32 And before him shall be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:133.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gathered all nations: and he shall separate them one</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:147.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from another, as a shepherd divideth his sheep from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:161.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the goats: 25:33 And he shall set the sheep on his right</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:175.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hand, but the goats on the left. 25:34 Then shall the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:189.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">King say unto them on his right hand, Come, ye</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:203.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">blessed of my Father, inherit the kingdom prepared</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:217.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for you from the foundation of the world: 25:35 For</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:231.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">I was an hungred, and ye gave me meat: I was thirsty,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:245.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and ye gave me drink: I was a stranger, and ye took</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:259.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">me in: 25:36 Naked, and ye clothed me: I was sick,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:273.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and ye visited me: I was in prison, and ye came unto</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:287.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">me. 25:37 Then shall the righteous answer him,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:301.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">saying, Lord, when saw we thee an hungred, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:315.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">fed thee? or thirsty, and gave thee drink?  25:38</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:329.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">When saw we thee a stranger, and took thee in? or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:343.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">naked, and clothed thee?  25:39 Or when saw we</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:357.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thee sick, or in prison, and came unto thee?  25:40</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:371.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">And the King shall answer and say unto them,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:385.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Verily I say unto you, Inasmuch as ye have done it</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:400.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto one of the least of these my brethren, ye have</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:414.05px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">done it unto me. 25:41 Then shall he say also unto</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.05px;top:427.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">them on the left hand, Depart from me, ye</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:443.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cursed, into everlasting fire, prepared for the devil and his angels: 25:42 For I was an hungred, and ye</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:457.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gave me no meat: I was thirsty, and ye gave me no drink: 25:43 I was a stranger, and ye took me not in:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:471.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">naked, and ye clothed me not: sick, and in prison, and ye visited me not. 25:44 Then shall they also</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:485.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">answer him, saying, Lord, when saw we thee an hungred, or athirst, or a stranger, or naked, or sick,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:499.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">or in prison, and did not minister unto thee?  25:45 Then shall he answer them, saying, Verily I say</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:513.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto you, Inasmuch as ye did it not to one of the least of these, ye did it not to me. 25:46 And these</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:527.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shall go away into everlasting punishment: but the righteous into life eternal.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:547.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">According to Jesus’ explanation of salvation here, his crucifixion is not necessary; baptism of the saved person is not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:561.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">necessary; even recognition of Jesus’ identity is not necessary, much less faith or belief in any doctrine other than</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:575.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">helping those in need.  On the other hand, turning away from those in need, which so-called Christians find easy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.36px;top:589.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">today, is condemned in terms just as clear.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:609.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.01px;top:714.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">38</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:30476px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background039.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:273.77px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">James the Just</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:45.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Who leads the Jerusalem Church after Jesus’ sudden, violent  death? According to Acts, it is Peter, but Paul lists</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:59.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">James prior to “Cephas” (Peter) and John as those considered "pillars" of the Jerusalem Church. Further, Eusebius</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:73.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">records that Clement of Alexandria wrote that Peter, James, and John chose James, the brother of Jesus, as bishop of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:87.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jerusalem. As is made clear in his Epistle, James emphasizes Jesus’ doctrine of salvation by ‘works.’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:384.91px;top:121.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from the Epistle of James</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:135.14px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-14/">:14 What doth it profit, my brethren, though a man say</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:149.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-14/">he hath faith, and have not works? can faith save him?</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:163.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-15/">15 If a brother or sister be naked, and destitute of daily</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:177.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-15/">food, 16 And one of you say unto them, Depart in</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:191.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-16/">peace, be ye warmed and filled; notwithstanding ye give</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:205.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-16/">them not those things which are needful to the body;</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:219.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-16/">what doth it profit? 17 Even so faith, if it hath not works,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:233.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-17/">is dead, being alone. 18 Yea, a man may say, Thou hast</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:247.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-18/">faith, and I have works: shew me thy faith without thy</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:261.53px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-18/">works, and I will shew thee my faith by my works. 19</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:275.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-19/">Thou believest that there is one God; thou doest well:</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:289.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-19/">the devils also believe, and tremble. 20 But wilt thou</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:303.53px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-20/">know, O vain man, that faith without works is dead? 21</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:317.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-21/">Was not Abraham our father justified by works, when</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:331.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-21/">he had offered Isaac his son upon the altar? 22 Seest</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:345.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-22/">thou how faith wrought with his works, and by works</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:359.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-22/">was faith made perfect? 23 And the scripture was</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:373.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-23/">fulfilled which saith, Abraham believed God, and it</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:387.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-23/">was imputed unto him for righteousness: and he was</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:401.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">called the Friend of God. </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-24/">24 Ye see then how that by works a man is justified, and not by faith only.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:415.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-25/">25 Likewise also was not Rahab the harlot justified by works, when she had received the messengers,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:429.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-25/">and had sent them out another way? 26 For as the body without the spirit is dead, so faith without</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:443.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/James-2-26/">works is dead also.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:457.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This epistle was specifically written to contradict Paul, who was then proselytizing salvation by faith</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:471.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">alone. James and Paul also differed over whether to preach to Gentiles, widening the rift in the early</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:485.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">church, as indicated in Galatians 2:9ff.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:505.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:301.01px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">39</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:31278px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background040.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul of Tarsus, an apocalyptic Pharisee of the diaspora</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:45.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">community in Asia Minor, initially feels that Christian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:59.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">claims that Jesus is the Messiah are absurd to the point</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:73.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of being blasphemous. He is very intelligent and well</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:87.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">read in the Septuagint (the source of all his quotations</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:101.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Scripture). He participates in the suppression of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:115.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christians and may well have been present at the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">martyrdom of St. Stephen. On the road to Damascus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:143.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he has a nervous breakdown, due probably to the echoes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:157.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Isaiah condemning oppression of the poor ringing in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:171.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">his ears, since early Christian communities were most</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:185.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">likely comprised largely of the socio-politically</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:199.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">disadvantaged.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.84px;top:213.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">His breakdown is likely also, considering his later hostility</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:227.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to the Jewish Law, a result of his view that Pharisaic obsession with minutiae of the Law of Moses is superfluous to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the central Biblical message of the Two Great Commandments to love God and one’s neighbor. During his seizure</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he has a vision of the resurrected Jesus from whom he learns “his gospel.” He then fastidiously avoids going to see</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">other Apostles for three years, during which time he formulates his message, the gist of which is as follows:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:284.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1. Jesus rose from the dead, hence he is blessed of God, not cursed as would be anyone “hanged upon a tree.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:298.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2. Since he is blessed, his death must have been directed by God; it cannot have been a random event.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:312.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3. His death must be a sacrifice; but he is blameless, so it must be a sacrifice for others.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:326.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4. Others must therefore be guilty, but of what? Ah, the sin of Adam (original sin) must have universal effect.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:340.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">5. How can we benefit from this sacrifice? Only by baptism, whereby we are cleansed of Adam’s sin and may</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:354.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">receive God’s grace.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:368.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">6. Is that enough? No, we must consciously accept and believe in Jesus’ sacrifice; otherwise we won’t be saved.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:54.00px;top:382.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">7. Isn’t it enough to help those in need, as Jesus taught in the Parable of the Sheep and Goats? No, if that were</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:397.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sufficient, then Jesus would not have been required to die on the cross.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:411.05px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This entire system of ideas was constructed to defend Paul’s cherished belief that Jesus’ crucifixion was necessary.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:424.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">All the rest of the elaborate tissue emerges from this one flawed tenet.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:439.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">When Paul encounters resistance from Jews who do not share his deviant reading of Jewish Scripture, he reacts by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:453.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">taking his message to Gentiles. That he was a convincing speaker is undeniable. In certain cases, people (e.g., his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:467.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">jailer) seem to have been “converted” without having the slightest understanding of what he preached.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:481.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Indeed, Paul himself could not willfully contradict Jesus’ teaching because he simply did not know Jesus’ teaching.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:495.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">When he wrote his Epistles (~50CE) there were as yet no gospels and he avoided contact with the Apostles.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:509.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">What his writings reflect  about Jesus is limited to: the fact that Jesus was Jewish, was born of a woman, had a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:523.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brother named James, taught his followers to pay their preachers and not to divorce, performed the Last Supper,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:537.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and was crucified. He never quotes Jesus, even when discussing an issue about which Jesus spoke convincingly . He</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:551.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">never says, “Jesus taught,” but always “I taught.” If we compare Jesus’ teachings to Paul’s, discrepancies are evident:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:565.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">While both Jesus and Paul were apocalypticists who taught love of God and of neighbor, Jesus taught turning the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:579.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">other cheek, while Paul bitterly attacked his enemies; Jesus spurned Mammon, while Paul sought and cultivated the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:593.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wealthy; Jesus felt disgust with the self-righteous, while Paul built a ‘righteous’ church bureaucracy; Jesus preached</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:607.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the imminence of the end, as did Paul at first, but when the end didn’t come, Paul adjusted his message; Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:621.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">associated with sinners, while Paul associated with “believers”; Jesus taught salvation through good works, while</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:635.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul taught salvation through baptism and faith; Jesus lived as a Jew, while Paul rejected the Law and lived “as a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:649.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Greek”; Jesus taught Jews to “follow the Law,” while Paul vehemently forbade  Gentile converts to follow the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:663.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Law.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:683.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:299.09px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">40</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:32080px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background041.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:218.21px;top:31.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Suppression of the Jamesian Ebionites</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:45.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">So were there any believers in the early days who followed the teachings of Jesus and James? Yes, the Ebionites (“the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:59.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">poor”) follow James, are observant of the Jewish Law and rites, stress poverty and good works, and regard Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:73.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Nazareth as “a prophet, the biological son of Mary and Joseph, who by virtue of his righteousness, was chosen by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:87.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">God to be a messianic prophet like Moses when he was anointed with the Holy Spirit at his baptism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:101.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by John.”  They rejected Jesus’ pre-existence, divinity,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:115.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">virgin birth, atoning death, and physical resurrection.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">They use only the gospel of Matthew starting at chapter</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:143.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3, revere James the brother of Jesus (James the Just),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:157.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and reject Paul the Apostle as an apostate from the Law.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:171.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">They place a special value on voluntary poverty.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:185.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">‘Ebionim’ is also among the terms used by the sect at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:199.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Qumran (possibly Essenes) that sought to separate</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:213.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">itself from the corruption of the Temple. The earliest</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:227.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reference to a group that might fit the description of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the later Ebionites appears in Justin Martyr's Dialogue</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with Trypho (c. 140), while Irenaeus (c. 180) was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">probably the first to use the term "Ebionites" to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:283.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">describe the ‘heretical judaizing sect,’ which he</span></div>
