<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:297.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">regarded as stubbornly clinging to the Law. (This first</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:311.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mention does not mean that they emerged in 180CE,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:325.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but only that they then became a problem for the proto-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:367.99px;top:337.73px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Heretic books burned by Papal decree</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:339.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Orthodox.)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:359.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:373.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">After James’ death, a struggle ensues between the followers of James (‘faith without works is dead’) and those of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:387.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul. The church in Jerusalem chooses Paul’s “gospel” and turns orthodox, likely because Paul’s version of salvation</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:401.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">requires a devoted, sacramental, priestly, paternalistic hierarchy (a church), while Jesus’ and James’ version does</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:415.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not. Anyone who attacks the prerogatives of the Church by asserting the teachings of Jesus and James is branded a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:430.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">heretic, which brings us to the great contest between Pelagius and Augustine of Hippo.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:450.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:637.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0041 Herod Agrippa (Herod the Great’s grandson, friend of the Emperor Claudius) takes over as king. A</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:651.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hasmonean, he shows reverence for local customs; the people have a brief respite of good government.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:667.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0044 Agrippa dies suddenly; Governors are back; relations deteriorate; rebellion and false prophets pop up:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:681.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Thelgas, the Egyptian.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:281.93px;top:697.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:300.53px;top:728.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">41</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:32882px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background042.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:233.69px;top:32.16px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Augustine of Hippo (354-430)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:46.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is best known for his ideas on the relationship between</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:60.24px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the will, grace, and predestination. Raised as a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:74.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christian by his mother, Monica, he reads Hortensius</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:88.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and becomes Manichaean. In 370 he begins a thirteen-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:102.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">year relationship with the mother (never named in his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:116.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">works) of his son, Adeodatus (born 372). In 383 he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:130.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">moves to Rome, is exposed to neo-Platonic idealism,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:144.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and rejects Manichaeism. His mother joins him in Milan,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:158.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">forces him to send his child’s mother away, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:172.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">arranges a marriage for him to a 10-year old Christian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:186.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">heiress. In 386 Augustine renounces his career and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:200.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">marriage, and is baptized by St. Ambrose. Augustine's</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:214.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">core ideas even after his reconversion still reflect</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:228.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Manichaean concepts: Hell, Elect and Reprobates,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:242.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hostility to the flesh and sexual activity, and dualistic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:256.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">theology. In 389, he writes Confessions, sells his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:270.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">patrimony, and gives the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:377.47px;top:270.53px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Consecration_of_Saint_Augustine">Consecration of Saint Augustine</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:284.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">money to the poor. In 391 he is drafted as priest at Thagaste, near Carthage. In 410, Rome is sacked by Visigoths,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:298.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and Christians are blamed for their unmanly, pacifist behavior, in answer to which he writes City of God.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:36.00px;top:312.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Pelagian Controversy:  Pelagius, a British monk, asserts that people are not born with a “sinful nature” and thus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:326.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">do not require the “cleansing” of infant baptism.  He claims that people can choose to live a good life or a bad life,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:340.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and can thus choose salvation or damnation. He sees in Jesus not an atoning death “to wash away the sins of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:354.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">world,” but merely a divine model of virtuous life. He considers death to be natural to all men (since baptism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:368.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">doesn’t confer immortality).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:382.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Like Pelagius, many early Church Fathers taught that humans have the power of free will and the choice over good</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:397.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and evil: Justin Martyr - "every created being is so constituted as to be capable of vice and virtue. For he can do</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:411.05px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">nothing praiseworthy, if he had not the power of turning either way." Theophilus   - "If, on the other hand, he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:425.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">would turn to the things of death, disobeying God, he would himself be the cause of death to himself. For God</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:439.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">made man free, and with power of himself." Irenaeus - "But man, being endowed with reason, and in this respect</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:453.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">similar to God, having been made free in his will, and with power over himself, is himself his own cause that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:467.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sometimes he becomes wheat, and sometimes chaff." Clement of Alexandria  - "We...have believed and are saved</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:481.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by voluntary choice." Before Pelagius, even Augustine suggested that the will is confronted by a rational choice</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:495.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">between a life spent in the pursuit of what is temporal, changing, and perishable, and a life spent in the pursuit of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:509.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">what is eternal, immutable, and incapable of being lost [De Libero Arbitrio I.7]; and that God's grace is "a reward for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:523.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">human assent,” that will is independent to choose good or evil, and that salvation is thus in the hands of the believer.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:537.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">However, as Pelagianism spreads rapidly, especially around Carthage, Augustine changes his tune and reacts to this</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:551.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">attack upon the sacraments by accusing Pelagius of heresy at the Council of Carthage in 418. Augustine’s logic is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:565.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">similar to Paul’s: if good deeds can save us, why did Jesus have to die on the cross? To defeat Pelagius and uphold</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:579.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Sacramental Church, Augustine devises a system whereby salvation is gained only by “irresistible” divine will;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:593.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">namely, that people have no choice. Likewise, damnation is the result of divine grace withheld, in which case people</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:607.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">again have no choice. “Grace irresistibly changes our will so that those chosen cannot reject it, and those from whom</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:621.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">it is withheld cannot be saved.”  [De Gratia et Libero Arbitrio xx and xxi]. Augustine is even pushed by the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:635.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">absurdity of his position to argue that unbaptized babies, and by extension miscarried or aborted babies, burn in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:649.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hell for all eternity. Also, misreading Genesis, Augustine maintains that death is a consequence of original sin (yet</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:663.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">it is curiously not remedied by baptism or Jesus’ crucifixion).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:45.00px;top:677.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In order to maintain its monopoly on the machinery of salvation, the Church endorses Augustine.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.69px;top:697.66px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:299.81px;top:728.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">42</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:33684px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background043.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:198.26px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Gospel (not </span><span class="cls_022">by</span><span class="cls_003"> Mark, but) </span><span class="cls_022">according to</span><span class="cls_003"> Mark</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The first Gospel is written - Jesus is portrayed as the misunderstood prophet (Adoptionism). In Codex</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Sinaiticus and Codex Vaticanus the gospel actually ends at 16:8, as noted by Eusebius and Jerome,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">though Irenaeus (200 CE) cites verse 19, demonstrating that the early Church Fathers probably made</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the addition in order to harmonize Mark with the other gospels.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:443.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mark 16:8 ‘And they went out quickly, and fled from the sepulchre; for they trembled and were</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:457.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">amazed: neither said they any thing to any man; for they were afraid.’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:473.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0065 Sources of Gospel stories: The Gospels are written by those inspired by the Holy Spirit (i.e.,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:487.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">IMAGINATION!). For example, when they read in Micah that the Messiah rose out of Egypt, of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:501.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">course the Spirit makes them think it must be Jesus who rose out of Egypt, so Matt 2:13 puts him in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:515.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Egypt.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:531.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Often gospel stories mirror those of the pagan faiths around them. For example, the immaculate</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:545.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conception of Plato, whose mother Perictione was impregnated by Apollo, who declared to Ariston,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:559.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to whom she was betrothed, the parentage of the child; the story of an evil serpent sent to ruin</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:574.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">paradise was taught to the Jews by the Babylonians during the Captivity; also, the ideas of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:588.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">resurrection, the immortality of the soul, and dualism were taught not by Jews, but by Persians and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:602.02px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">incorporated into the Judaeo-Christian mythology during the Persian period of occupation.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:618.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.29px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">43</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:34486px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background044.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:121.34px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Where is God? The First Jewish-Roman War - The Second Temple is destroyed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judaism again loses its raison d’être. This is a huge shock to the fundamental system of Judaism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:226.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0070 Diaspora is considered the ultimate punishment for people fallen away from God, but the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:240.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian community is a success. With Hellenism, borders disappear, and Jews follow business</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:254.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">opportunities, and actually convert some Gentiles. Because Babylon is outside the Hellenist world, its</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:268.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jewish community keeps its exclusionist identity. Philo: ‘The diaspora is the realization of God’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:282.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">promise to Abraham.’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:298.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0070 Rabbis: With the Temple gone - who’s in charge? Yohanan Ben Zakkai (30 BC-90 AD) -</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:312.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">‘When in doubt, plant a tree.’ Ritual is modified, as is use of the shofar, which thitherto could only be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:326.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sounded in the Temple. The new rabbinical model is based not on birth, but vocation. Rabbis are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:340.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mobile and establish local centers; the nature of ritual is changed from sacrifice to reading and prayer</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:355.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in synagogues. Then Rabban Gamaliel (Acts 5:34) establishes a bureaucracy, supports Rome, and is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:369.05px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">named patriarch. Prayer is introduced into the synagogues, especially the Amida Prayer, including a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:383.09px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">benediction against the minim (Christian heretics?). Unlike the time of the destruction of the First</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:397.13px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Temple, Jews are now more ready to expect the End - Where is God? Was God defeated? Is there</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:411.17px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a new covenant? People are ready for extreme means and ends.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:427.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0080 Gnosticism - Non-rabbinical Jewish sects and early Christian sects of Gnosticism develop, out</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:441.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the remains of apocalyptic  expectations after the fall of Jerusalem (70 AD), which shatters the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:455.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hopes of the coming of God's kingdom on earth and leads to a rejection of the world. Within early</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:469.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christianity, the teachings of Paul and John may have been a starting point for Gnostic ideas, with a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:483.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">growing emphasis on the opposition between flesh and spirit, the value of charisma, and the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:497.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">disqualification of the Jewish law. Tertullian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:511.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">calls Paul "the apostle of the heretics," because</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:525.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul's writings were attractive to Gnostics, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:539.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">interpreted in a Gnostic way, while Jewish</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:553.39px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christians felt he strayed from the Jewish roots</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:567.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Christianity. Paul wrote to the Corinthian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:581.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">church members as "having knowledge."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:595.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Gnostic ideas find a Jewish variation in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:609.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mystical study of Kabbalah.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:624.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0080 The Gospel according to Matthew - Jesus as the Jewish Messiah</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0085 The Gospel according to Luke and the Acts of the Apostles - Jesus as the Universal Savior</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:656.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0090 The Gospel according to John - Jesus as The Word made Flesh</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:672.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:307.85px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">44</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:35288px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background045.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:257.93px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Early Church Fathers</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Writings of the Apostolic Fathers: First Clement (c. 120 CE)- The Church of Rome intrudes in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:97.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Corinth; Ignatius' Letters (c. 120 CE) - seven letters regarding his going to Rome to be martyred;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Letter(s) of Polycarp to the Philippians (c.125 CE) - against Docetists and Resurrection-deniers;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Martyrdom of Polycarp (c. 155 CE) - "Away with the atheists!"</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0115 Jewish Rebellion in Egypt and Cyrene, led by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(king?) Lucas/Andreas</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0130 Papias Bishop of Hieropolis. (c. 70-c. 155 CE)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christian apologists for early gospel dates rely on</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the slimmest of evidence, including a very late</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">third-hand testimony of a late second-hand</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">testimony that "Mark" had written a narrative,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">supposedly based on the experiences of Peter as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">related by the apostle himself. In the fourth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">century, Church historian Eusebius quotes Papias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:283.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Hierapolis as referring to the "presbyter John."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:297.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Regarding the bishop of Hierapolis, the Catholic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Encyclopedia says, "Of Papias's life nothing is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">known." According to Eusebius—in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">disagreement with Irenaeus, who suggests Papias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">had known the apostle John—Papias has no direct</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">acquaintance with any of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:383.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">apostles: …Papias himself in the preface to his Exposition of the Sayings of the Lord makes clear that he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:397.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was never a hearer or eyewitness of the holy apostles, and tells us that he learnt the essentials of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faith from their former pupils. The assumption that the "presbyter John" with whom Papias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">apparently had a relationship is the apostle John is evidently incorrect. Many of Papias' remarks,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">according to Eusebius, involve miracles, such as the raising of the dead, which test one’s credulity.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Papias is one of the only pieces of evidence Christian apologetics offers as to the dating of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:468.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gospels—yet, his testimony concerning these writings of Mark and Matthew is not only second-hand</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:482.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but also too late to possess any value as concerns the earliest of the gospels dates. Moreover, Papias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:496.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">speaks only about a narrative by Mark, which by no means conclusively refers to the canonical Mark as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:510.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">we have it. Nor is the Aramaic gospel of Matthew the same as the canonical Matthew.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0132-0135 Hadrian plans to rebuild Jerusalem as a Hellene city, Aelia Capitolina. Fears of pagan worship</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:540.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">on Temple Mount (just as those that preceded the Machabean rebellion) occurring 70 years after the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">destruction of the Temple (just as the Temple was rebuilt in 516, 70 years after its destruction in 586)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:568.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inspire Nasi (“king”) Simon Bar Kochba to rise as a military Messiah against the Evil Empire</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:582.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Rome). A definitive defeat was required before Jews could resign themselves to a “Judaism of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:596.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">possible.” He is, however, not supported by any rabbis except Akiva, and the revolt fails. Jews are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:610.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">now banned from Jerusalem, and Judea is renamed Syria-Palestina. The Messianic model becomes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:624.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spiritual rather than military for Jews. The Babylonian rabbinic community takes precedence. What</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:638.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">about Jews living outside the Holy Land? Philo of Alexandria is an example of successful adaptation.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:654.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.05px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">45</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:36090px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background046.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:269.33px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Age of Heresy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0144 Marcionism - Marcion believes Jesus is the savior sent by God, and Paul is his chief apostle, but he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rejects the Hebrew Bible and God of the Old Testament as a tyrant or demiurge. Marcionists believe</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that the God of the Old Testament is a separate and lower entity than the all-forgiving God of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">New Testament. This belief is similar to Gnostic theology - both are dualistic, that is, they posit</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Manichaean) opposing gods, forces, or principles: one higher, spiritual, and "good," and the other</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">lower, material, and "evil." This dualism stands in contrast to other Christian and Jewish views that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"evil" has no independent existence, being merely an absence of "good." Marcion’s canon consists of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">eleven books: an abridged Gospel of Luke and ten Pauline epistles. The premise of Marcionism is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that many of the teachings of Jesus are incompatible with the actions of the Hebrew God.  He further</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">regards the arguments of Paul regarding law and gospel, wrath and grace, works and faith, flesh and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spirit, sin and righteousness, death and life, as the essence of religious truth.  Marcionites hold that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the God of the Hebrew Bible (known to Gnostics as Yaltabaoth) is inconsistent, jealous, wrathful and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">genocidal, and that the material world he created is defective, a place of suffering; the God who made</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:265.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">such a world is a bungling or malicious </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demiurge">demiurge.</A><span class="cls_003">  Marcionism shows the influence of <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic">Hellenistic</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:279.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">philosophy on Christianity, by presenting a moral critique of the Old Testament from the standpoint</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:293.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platonism">Platonism.</A> According to Harnack, the sect may have led other Christians to introduce a formal</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:307.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">statement of beliefs into their liturgy and to formulate a canon of authoritative </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred_text">Scripture</A> of their own,</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:321.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thus </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Development_of_the_New_Testament_canon">eventually producing the current canon of the New Testament.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0150 Justin Martyr (c. 150 CE) As proof of the existence of the gospels prior to the end of the second</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">century, it is claimed that Church father Justin Martyr included 268 "quotations of the New</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Testament" in his First Apology  (cf. New Evidence that Demands a Verdict by Josh McDowell).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0180 Irenaeus (fl. 180 CE) "Father of the Catholic Canon." The four canonical gospels were not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mentioned or named as such by anyone until the time of Church Father Irenaeus, Bishop of Lyons. In</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:409.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Against All Heresies (III, 11.8), Irenaeus is the first to name the canonical gospels and give reasons for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">their inclusion in the New Testament.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0180 Theophilus (Luke’s Theophilus?), Bishop of Antioch (Luke’s home town), is the first Church</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">father clearly to discuss the canonical gospels.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:469.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0200 The Mishna, a rabbinical guidebook, is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:484.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">compiled by Nasi Judah the Patriarch; later, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:498.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Talmud (ancient rabbinic writings) is written:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:512.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">one in Babylon (more popular), and one in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jerusalem, as a commentary on the Mishna.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:542.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0200 Docetism (Marcionism) - Docetists maintain that Jesus’ human form is an illusion, as testified by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:556.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the uncanonical Gospel of Peter. This system of beliefs is condemned by Polycarp and Serapion.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0220 Sabellianism - God the Father, Jesus Christ, and the Holy Spirit are three different modes or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">aspects of one monadic God, as perceived by the believer, rather than three distinct persons within the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Godhead - that there are no real or substantial differences between the three, such that there is no</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:614.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">substantial identity for the Spirit or the Son. At the Arroyo Seco World Wide Camp Meeting, near</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:628.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Los Angeles, in 1913, </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadians">Canadian</A><span class="cls_003"> evangelist <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R.E._McAlister">R.E. McAlister</A> states at a baptismal service that the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:642.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">apostles baptized in the name of Jesus only and not in the triune Name of Father, Son, and Holy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:656.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Spirit (Sabellianism is not dead!).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:672.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.09px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">46</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:36892px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background047.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:251.21px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Real Story of Christmas</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“Christmas” is a non-Biblical celebration, that is to say, it is mentioned nowhere in the Bible, was not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">practiced by the Early Church, and Church Father Origen (c. 184-c. 253 CE) declared it a pagan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">practice and its celebration a sin.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The date of Jesus’ birth is a matter of speculation,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but the four Biblical hints do not favor December</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">25: first, the Star of Bethlehem, if a juncture of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Venus and Jupiter, occurred on June 17, 2 BCE,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">while that of Jupiter and Saturn occurred in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">October 7 BCE; second, shepherds tend their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:213.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">flocks “in the field” (Luke 2:8 </span><span class="cls_007">αγραυλουντες</span><span class="cls_003">)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:227.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from May to October, not in December; third,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:241.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zacharias’ service as Priest (Luke 1:8-11, 23-24,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:255.41px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">26-27)  indicates the birth of John the Baptist in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:269.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">March, and that of Jesus six months later; finally,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:283.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">censuses were forbidden in December, as that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:297.53px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was a difficult travel month (Ezra 10:9-13).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:311.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">October might fit, but not December.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:327.53px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">On the other hand, the Saturnalia, in honor of a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:341.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman agricultural deity, with drunken reveling,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:355.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gift-giving, and the reversal of roles between</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:369.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">slaves and masters, was celebrated each year until</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:383.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">around December 23. Also, in 274 CE, Roman</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:397.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Emperor Aurelian declared December 25 to be a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:411.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">festival in honor of “the birth of Sol Invictus,”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:425.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(winter solstice as the birth of the sun) a Mithraic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:439.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sun-god cult characterized by handshakes and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:453.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ritual meals before altars in underground temples.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:469.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In 313 CE, in an effort to unite his dissolving Empire, Emperor Constantine issued the Edict of Milan,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:483.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">declaring religious tolerance for Christianity, and later presided over the Council of Nicaea in 325 CE.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:497.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">As masses of Romans now converted to Christianity, they refused to give up their celebratory feasts at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:511.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Solstice. A moral debate raged among the clergy, some of whom felt that fallen humankind needed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:525.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a season of abandonment and excess (from which they could be gradually weaned), as long as it was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:539.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">carried on under the umbrella of Christian supervision, while others argued that all vestiges of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:553.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">paganism must be expunged. The Church compromised by recognizing December 25 as the nativity</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:568.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not of the Sun-god, but of the Son of God. In 742 CE, though, St. Boniface complained to Pope</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:582.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zacharias that the Franks and Germans, whom he was trying to convince to give up their pagan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:596.14px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">carnivals, had witnessed such celebrations in the shadow of St. Peter’s itself!</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:612.10px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Over subsequent centuries, Christmas absorbed further pagan symbols from Germans (Yule logs),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:626.14px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Scandinavians (decorated evergreen trees) and Druids (mistletoe). Reformation Protestants tried</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reforming Christmas but had little impact. In 1659 English Puritans outlawed Christmas as unchristian,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:654.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but it proved so popular that it was “restored” in 1681.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:670.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.57px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">47</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:37694px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background048.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:283.49px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">More Heresies!</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0276 Manichaeism - Manichaeism teaches an elaborate </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dualistic_cosmology">dualistic cosmology</A><span class="cls_003"> describing the <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conflict_between_good_and_evil">struggle</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">between a </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goodness_and_value_theory">good,</A><span class="cls_003"> spiritual world of light; and an <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evil">evil,</A> material world of darkness. Through an ongoing</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">process that takes place in human history, light is gradually removed from the world of matter and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">returned to the world of light, whence it came. Its beliefs are rooted in Zoroastrian dualism preserved</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gnostic">gnostic</A> religious movements. Manichaeism spreads with extraordinary speed both east and west. It</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reaches Rome through the apostle Psattiq by 280 CE, via </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt">Egypt,</A><span class="cls_003"> where it flourishes in the <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fayum">Fayum</A> area</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">c. 290. Manichaean monasteries exist in Rome in 312 during the time of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Miltiades">Pope Miltiades.</A> <span class="cls_010"> </span><span class="cls_003">In 296,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</A> decrees against the Manichaeans: "We order that their organizers and leaders be subject to</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the final penalties and condemned to the fire with their abominable scriptures." This results in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">martyrdom for many in Egypt and North Africa. In 354, </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilary_of_Poitiers">Hilary of Poitiers</A> writes that the Manichaean</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faith is a significant force in southern Gaul. In 381, Christians request that </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodosius_I">Theodosius I</A> strip</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Manichaeans of their civil rights. He issues a decree of death for Manichaean monks in 382.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0300 Arianism - “Jesus was begotten by and is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">subordinate to the Father,” a belief held today by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jehovah’s Witnesses.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0325 The First Council of Nicaea is summoned to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">resolve a disagreements arising from within the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church_of_Alexandria">Church of Alexandria</A> over Arianism:  whether</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Son was 'begotten' by the Father from his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">own being, and therefore had no beginning, or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">else was created out of nothing, and therefore had</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a beginning. This hyper-intellectualization of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christianity allows total control over the message,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and of course the loser of the debate, Arius, is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">banished.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0350 Donatism - Elements of the Church attack</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">apostate clergy who had collaborated with the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:468.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman persecutors as unworthy to administer</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:482.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sacraments. </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</A> campaigns</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:498.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">against Donatism as bishop, and through his efforts, orthodoxy gains the upper hand. According to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:512.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Augustine, sacramental validity is a property of the priesthood independent of the individual character</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:526.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the priest. Influenced by the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Testament">Old Testament,</A> he believes in discipline as a means of education. In his</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:540.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">letter to Vincentius, Augustine uses the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Testament">New Testament Parable of the Great Banquet</A> to justify using</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">force against the Donatists: "You are of the opinion that no one should be compelled to follow</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:568.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">righteousness; and yet you read that the householder said to his servants, 'Whomsoever ye shall find,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:582.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">compel them to come in.'" The Church thereafter conveniently uses Augustine's texts to justify the use</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:596.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of force in the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_pagans_in_the_late_Roman_Empire">persecution of pagan religions,</A><span class="cls_003"> of heretics by the <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inquisition">Inquisition,</A> and of Native American</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:610.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_religion">religions.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:626.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The early reformers </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wycliffe">John Wycliffe</A> (d. 1384), who teaches that the moral corruption of priests</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">invalidates their offices and sacraments, and </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Hus">Jan Hus</A> (d. 1415), who argues that a prelate's moral</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:654.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">character determines his ecclesiastical authority, are accused of Donatism and condemned as </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy">heret</A>ics at</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:668.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Constance">Council of Constance</A> (1414-8).</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.45px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">48</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:38496px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background049.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0367 Athenasius, bishop of Alexandria, determines the canonical Scriptures of New Testament; the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:81.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Gnostic Nag Hamadi text of the Gospel of Thomas is hidden by Gnostics shortly thereafter.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0381 Monophysitism maintains that after the union of the divine and the human in the person of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_Christ">Jesus</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_Christ">Christ,</A><span class="cls_003"> he had only a single "nature" which was divine. Monophysitism is contrasted to <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyophysitism">duophysitism,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">which maintains that Christ maintained two natures, one divine and one human after incarnation.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Monophysitism is born in the theological </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_of_Alexandria">"School</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_of_Alexandria">of Alexandria,</A>" which begins its Christological</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">analysis with the (divine) eternal Son or Word</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of God and seeks to explain how this eternal</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Word became incarnate as a man — in contrast to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_of_Antioch">"School of Antioch</A>" (birthplace of</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nestorianism">Nestorianism,</A> the antithesis of Monophysitism),</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">which instead begins with the (human) Jesus of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Gospels and seeks to explain how this man</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:265.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">became united with the eternal Word in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:279.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Incarnation. Accepted by the Sees of Rome,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:293.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Constantinople, and Antioch, the Chalcedonian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:307.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">settlement (451CE) encounters strong resistance</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:321.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in Alexandria (and in Egypt generally), leading</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:335.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ultimately to the schism between the Oriental</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:349.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Orthodox churches (which reject Chalcedon) on</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:363.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the one hand, and the so-called </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalcedonian">Chalcedonian</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:377.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">churches on the other. There are two major</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:391.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">doctrines that can indisputably be called</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:361.39px;top:401.81px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">St. Dioscorus (left), Pope of Alexandria</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:405.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"monophysite":</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:83.18px;top:421.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(1) </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollinarianism">Apollinarianism</A> holds that Christ had a human body and human "living principle," but that the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:436.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logos_(Christianity)">Divine Logos</A><span class="cls_003"> took the place of the <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nous">nous</A> (mind). Apollinarianism is condemned as a heresy at the First</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:450.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ecumenical Council of Constantinople in 381. (2) </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eutychianism">Eutychianism</A> holds that the human and divine</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:463.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">natures of Christ were fused into one new single nature: His human nature was "dissolved like a drop of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:478.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">honey in the sea." Eutychianism is condemned at the Ecumenical Council of Chalcedon in 451, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:492.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">again at the non-chalcedonian Third Council of Ephesus in 475.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:508.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0420 Nestorianism - </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyophysite">dyophysitism: "Jesus</A> Christ, who is not identical with the Son but personally</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:522.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">united with the Son, who lives in him, is one </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypostasis_(philosophy_and_religion)">hypostasis</A> and one nature: human."</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:538.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.45px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">49</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:39298px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background050.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:264.65px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Into the Middle Ages</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0754 The Donation of Constantine - In 751 Aistulf, king of the Lombards (a Scandinavian horde),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conquers what remains of the Byzantine Empire in northern Italy and demands the submission of Pope</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Stephen II in Rome. In France, Pepin the Short, Mayor of the Palace of Neustria and Austrasia and a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman Catholic, deposes the last Merovingian king and claims the throne as King of the Franks, yet</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">lacks consensus for his rule. Stephen is in desperate need of an ally against the Lombards and so</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">approaches Pepin with the promise of monarchical legitimacy in return for his support. The Donation</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Constantine, by which the Emperor Constantine in 315 (or 317) gave to Pope Sylvester I the right to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">temporal rule over Western Europe, is likely forged for the occasion. Stephen, by the authority vested</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in the Donation, anoints Pepin King of the Franks in a ceremony recalled in French coronation rites</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">down to 1792. Pepin returns the favor by granting Stephen the Lombard territories he takes in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">northern and central Italy (the Rome-Ravenna Corridor that becomes the Papal States). In 778, Pope</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hadrian refers to the Donation in requesting further land-grants from Charlemagne. The forgery is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">exposed by Latinist scholar Lorenzo Valla in 1440, though doubts as to its authenticity had been</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:265.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">voiced by Emperor Otto III as early as 1001.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:217.13px;top:582.43px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Constantine (right) delivers the West to Sylvester</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:595.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">0950 Bogomilism (Cathars, Albigensians) is a dualist form of neo-Gnosticism that rejects ecclesiastical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:609.82px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hierarchy, and professes that God created the soul, while Satan created the body.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:625.78px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1150 St Anselm -Theology is "faith seeking understanding"</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:641.86px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.17px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">50</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:40100px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background051.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:277.37px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Where’s Waldo?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1173 Waldensians - Wealthy merchant </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Waldo">Peter Waldo</A><span class="cls_003"> gives away his property and preaches <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apostolic_poverty">apostolic</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apostolic_poverty">poverty</A><span class="cls_003"> as the way to <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfection">perfection.</A> He teaches that: temporal offices and dignities are not meant for</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">preachers of the Gospel; that saints’ relics are simply rotten bones which belonged to one knew not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">whom; that to go on pilgrimage serves no end, save to empty one's purse; that meat might be eaten any</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">day; that holy water is no more efficacious than rain water; and that prayer in a barn is just as effectual as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that offered in a church.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Waldensians are accused of having scoffed at the doctrine of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transubstantiation">transubstantiation,</A> and of having spoken</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">blasphemously of the Catholic Church as the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whore_of_Babylon">harlot of the Apocalypse.</A> They reject what they perceive</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as the idolatry of the Catholic Church and consider the Pope the Antichrist of Rome. They believe in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">such issues as the universal priesthood, preaching the gospel in the vulgar tongue, and taking up</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">voluntary poverty. The Catholic Church views the Waldensians as heretical, and in 1184 at the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod_of_Verona">Synod</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synod_of_Verona">of Verona,</A><span class="cls_003"> under the auspices of <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Lucius_III">Pope Lucius III,</A> they are excommunicated. Pope Innocent III goes</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">even further during the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_Lateran_Council">Fourth Lateran Council</A> in 1215, officially denouncing the Waldensians as</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy">heretics.</A><span class="cls_003"> In 1211 more than 80 Waldensians are burned as heretics at <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strasbourg">Strasbourg,</A> launching several</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">centuries of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Inquisition">persecution</A> that nearly destroy the movement. The group is nearly annihilated in the</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">seventeenth century and is confronted with organized and generalized discrimination in the centuries</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that followed.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">St Augustine taught that error has no rights. He cited biblical texts to justify the use of compulsion,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">notably Luke 14:16-23. Had not Christ himself blinded St Paul in order to make him see the true light?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">According to Augustine, coercion using “great violence” was justified. He made a distinction between</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unbelievers, who persecuted because of cruelty, and Christians, who persecuted because of love. A war</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to preserve or restore the unity of the Church was a just war, a bellum Deo auctore, a war waged by God</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">himself.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:228.77px;top:580.99px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">‘Christian love’ for the Waldensians in 1655</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:139.94px;top:593.11px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">from Samuel Moreland History of the Evangelical Churches of the Valleys of Piedmont. 1658</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:117.98px;top:605.14px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">The woman being tortured to death here is Anna, daughter of Giovanni Charboniere of La Torre.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:616.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The American Waldensian Society declares their mission to be to "proclaim the Christian Gospel, serve</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:630.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the marginalized, promote </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_justice">social justice,</A><span class="cls_003"> foster <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-religious">inter-religious</A> work, and advocate respect for religious</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">diversity and freedom of conscience."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:660.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:310.73px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">51</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:40902px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background052.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:287.57px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Inquisitions</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">are  institutions of the Catholic Church established to combat heresy, started in 1184 in France to root out</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Cathars and Waldensians in Southern France. In the papal bull Ad Extirpanda of 1252, Pope Innocent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">IV explicitly authorizes the use of torture to elicit confessions from suspected heretics. Inquisitions</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">were largely abolished after the Napoleonic Wars in Europe, but the office still exists in the Catholic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Church, though now called the Congregation of the Doctrine of the Faith. Most sentences seem to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have consisted of penances like wearing a cross sewn on one's clothes, going on pilgrimage, etc., though</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unrepentant heresy was often punished by burning at the stake.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:183.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Spanish Inquisition</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Inquisitions occur in all lands and colonies where the Catholic Church has authority (except England and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Castille), of which the most notorious is the Spanish Inquisition. The Iberian Peninsula in 1492 consists</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of territories recently reconquered from the Muslims and still retains strong Muslim and Jewish</span></div>
