<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">influence.  Muslims and Jews are given the choice of leaving, converting, or dying. Many stay and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">convert, though the Christian authorities doubt that all these conversos will suddenly become and remain</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">orthodox Roman Catholics. So this Inquisition has a special socio-political basis as well as fundamental</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religious motives. The last execution of the Spanish Inquisition occurs in 1826 when Cayetano Ripoll is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">garroted for teaching Deism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman Inquisition</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:329.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">After the Protestant Reformation explodes onto the scene, Catholic authorities become suspicious of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:343.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">vary Renaissance humanism that they earlier encouraged. In 1542 Pope Paul III establishes the Roman</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Inquisition to examine and proscribe errors and false doctrines. The most famous case it tries is that of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Galileo Galilei in 1633, for claiming that the sun is the center of the solar system. Galileo is found</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“vehemently suspect of heresy,” is threatened with torture if he does not recant his teachings; he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:399.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">recants, and is kept under house arrest until his death in 1642</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:148.34px;top:658.42px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Galileo interrogated by Cardinal John Bellarmine by Joseph-Nicolas Robert-Fleury</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:671.74px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:310.01px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">52</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:41704px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background053.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:294.17px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Witches</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The medieval church initially condemns belief in witches as a pagan superstition, but folk beliefs refuse to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">die. Local folk practice often mix chants, incantations, and prayers to the saints to ward off storms,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">protect cattle, or ensure a good harvest. Bonfires on Midsummer's Eve are intended to deflect natural</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">catastrophes or the influence of fairies, ghosts, and witches. The punishment for evil witchcraft is death,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but there are few prosecutions because of the Law of Talion, which stipulates that if the accused witch is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not found guilty, the accuser will pay the penalty of death. The difficulty of proving witchcraft is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sufficient to discourage frivolous accusations. In the 1230’s, however, Inquisitors, who accuse on behalf</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the Church rather than an individual and are thus free of the restrictions of the Law of Talion, link</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">heresy to magic. Before 1252, there is only about one prosecution per year. Then Inquisitors,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:209.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">authorized by Pope Innocent IV, begin to use torture to interrogate heretic magicians. When a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:223.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">suspected witch is reported to the Inquisitors, the individual is interrogated. If no confession is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:237.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">forthcoming, torture is employed, and the accused starts to confess to almost anything, and to accuse</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:251.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">other “members” of their “sabbat” (coven).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">From 1375 -1435 there is a marked increase in prosecutions, and treatises on witchcraft begin to appear,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">possibly in answer to the upheavals of the era - the Black Death (1347), the Hundred Years' War</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(1337-1453), the Little Ice Age (~1500-1700), and the Protestant Reformation (1517) - and these folk</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">superstitions percolate up into Church leadership. Still, as late as 1484, local German church officials are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:323.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reluctant to participate in the Inquisition, and one even expels Dominican priest Heinrich Kramer from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">his diocese in Innsbruck for making false accusations. In his influential book Malleus Maleficarum,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">published in 1487,Kramer expresses his beliefs that witchcraft is responsible for bad weather and that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">women are inherently susceptible to Satanic seduction because of their raging libido.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1500-1700 is the Golden Age for witch trials. By 1500 the concept of witches is well defined and widely</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">accepted, being written about by recognized intellectual authorities of the age (including English king</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">James I). Any misfortune which occurs, such a barn burning down, or the death of a child, or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">childlessness itself, can be ascribed to dark magic, and anyone who has a grudge against the victim of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">misfortune is under suspicion. As always, the most vulnerable are most suspect, and the most</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">vulnerable tend to be older women dependent upon the charity of others, most likely because of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:466.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">death of a husband. If one spurns the advances of a beggar and returns home to find ones barn burnt</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:480.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">down, the connection is clear. The fact that many of these women are emotionally fragile and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:494.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sometimes confess merely for the attention only reinforces the community’s fears. Women are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:508.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">considered to be intellectually and morally inferior, and on that account bitter. Witches are also</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:522.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">associated with a hunger for the flesh of infants,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:536.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">having animal familiars who aid in their fiendish</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:550.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">plans, a special mark of their bodies that signifies</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:564.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">their pact with Satan, and membership in a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:578.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“synagogue” or “sabbat” of witches who</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:592.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">participate in sexual orgies with demonic spirits.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:608.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The last witch executed in Europe is Anna Goeldin,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:622.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">decapitated on 13 June 1782 in Zurich after she</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:636.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">confesses, under torture, to a pact with Satan.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:650.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Her execution is described in the press as judicial</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:409.63px;top:662.62px" class="cls_008"><span class="cls_008">Anna Goeldin</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:664.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">murder.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:680.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:310.49px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">53</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:42506px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background054.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:288.17px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joan of Arc</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1260 Thomas Aquinas, a sage of scholasticism, proves that authorities agree even when they don't. In the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">14th century Realists (“reality is Platonic forms”) and Nominalists (“reality is what we sense”)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">challenge Aquinas’ argument that god is inscrutable.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1381 Lollardy is a religion of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_translations_in_the_Middle_Ages">vernacular scripture.</A> Lollards oppose many practices of the Catholic Church.</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Followers of John Wycliff believe that the bible is the only valid source of doctrine and pertinent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">measure of legitimacy." They do not believe the church practices of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baptism">baptism</A><span class="cls_003"> and <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacrament_of_Penance">confession</A> are</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">necessary for </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvation_in_Christianity">salvation.</A><span class="cls_003"> They consider praying to saints and <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iconoclasm">honoring of their images</A> to be a form of</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">idolatry. Oaths, fasting, and prayers for the dead are thought to have no </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wycliffe%27s_Bible">scriptural basis.</A> They have a</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">poor opinion of the trappings of the Catholic Church, including holy bread, holy water, bells, organs,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and church buildings. They reject the value of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indulgence#Early_and_medieval_beliefs">papal pardons.</A> Special vows are considered to be in</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conflict with the divine order established by Jesus and are regarded as </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anathema#Catholicism">anathema.</A> They are opposed to</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">pilgrimages and saint worship, they deny the doctrine of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transubstantiation">transubstantiation,</A><span class="cls_003"> and demand an <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_translations_into_English">English</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_translations_into_English">translation of the Scriptures.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1431 Joan of Arc, born a peasant at Domremy in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">northeast France, is considered a heroine of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">France for her role during the Hundred Years’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">War. Joan claims to have received visions of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Archangel Michael, Saint Margaret, and Saint</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Catherine of Alexandria instructing her to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">recover France from English domination. The</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unanointed King Charles VII reluctantly sends</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joan to the Siege of Orleans as part of a relief</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">army. She gains prominence when the siege is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">lifted only nine days later. Several additional</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">swift victories lead to Charles VII's consecration</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">at Rheims. This paves the way for the final</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">French victory.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:468.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">On 23 May 1430, she is captured Burgundians. She</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:482.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is sold to the English after Charles VII refuses to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:496.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ransom her, put on trial by the Inquisitor of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:510.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">North France Jean Lemaitre for witchcraft</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:524.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">because she wore male clothing, and burnt at the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:538.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">stake at about nineteen years of age.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:554.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Her attribution of Divine Guidance annoys</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:568.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Church leaders, but she is finally canonized in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:582.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1920, though as late as 1902, Papal Consistors cite</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:596.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">her capture as proof that her claims that she was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:610.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sent by God are false, and refuse to place her in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:624.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Calendar of Saints.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:296.21px;top:641.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">______</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.05px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">54</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:43308px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background055.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.81px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Martin Luther</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1517 Luther publishes his 95 Theses - and formulates a creed whereby humans are considered to be deeply</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:97.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">corrupt, powerless to save themselves, and justified only through god's grace. The individual relates</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">directly to god (without the intercession of a Church); that church is a place for sermons, not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sacraments; and that only the Bible has authority (not the writings of Church Fathers). Protestant</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">reformers Martin Luther and John Calvin agree with the post-Pelagian Augustine that Original Sin</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">completely destroys liberty </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_depravity">(total depravity</A>), thereby presuming a lack of free will.</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Luther was, unfortunately, also a vicious anti-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:183.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Semite. In On the Jews and their Lies he asks:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"What shall we Christians do with this rejected</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and condemned people, the Jews":</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"First, to set fire to their synagogues or schools …</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">so that God might see that we are Christians …</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:257.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Second, I advise that their houses also be razed.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:273.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Third, I advise that all their prayer books and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:287.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Talmudic writings …be taken from them.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:303.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fourth, I advise that their rabbis be forbidden to teach henceforth on pain of loss of life and limb …</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:319.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fifth, I advise that safe-conduct on the highways be abolished completely for the Jews…</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:335.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Sixth, I advise that … all cash and treasure of silver and gold be taken from them …</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Seventh, I recommend putting a flail, an ax, a hoe, a spade, a distaff, or a spindle into the hands of young,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">strong Jews and Jewesses and letting them earn their bread in the sweat of their brow … But if we are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:379.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">afraid that they might harm us, … then let us eject them forever from the country …"</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:395.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">A little further on, he writes "we are at fault in not slaying them."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">As a result of Luther’s influence, his Prince, John Frederick I, Elector of Saxony, in 1543 revoked</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">concessions granted to his Jewish community; John of Brandenburg-Küstrin repealed the safe conduct</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Jews in his territories; Luther's followers sacked the synagogue of Berlin in 1572 and in the following</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">years the Jews were driven out of Brandenburg and several other German Lutheran states.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:469.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Shortly after the Kristallnacht, Martin Sasse, Bishop of the Evangelical Lutheran Church in Thuringia,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:484.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">published a compendium of Luther’s writings; Sasse: "On November 10, 1938, on Luther's birthday,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:498.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the synagogues are burning in Germany."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The city of Nuremberg presented a first edition of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">On the Jews and their Lies to Julius Streicher,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:542.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">editor of the Nazi newspaper Der Stürmer, on his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:556.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">birthday in 1937. It was publicly exhibited in a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:570.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">glass case at the Nuremberg rallies. On</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:584.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">December 17, 1941, seven Lutheran regional</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:598.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">church confederations issued a statement</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:612.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">agreeing with the policy of forcing Jews to wear</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:626.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the yellow badge, "since after his bitter</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">experience Luther had strongly suggested</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:654.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">preventive measures against the Jews and their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:668.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">expulsion from German territory."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:403.15px;top:669.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Julius Streicher</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:684.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:310.13px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">55</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:44110px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background056.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:262.97px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1545 Council of Trent</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Catholic Church responds to the Protestant</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">surge in Northern Europe with reform and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religious wars. Jesuits open universities teaching</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Scholasticism infused with Renaissance</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">humanism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1630 Herbert of Cherbury contrasts revealed/positive religion to natural religion. Natural religion is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">universal, rational, and compatible with nature. Organized religion is by its nature corrupt.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1640~ Descartes asserts "natural reason," as the highest intellectual authority: ”cogito ergo sum.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:201.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1666 Philipp Spener - The Pietists argue for spiritual and moral regeneration to overcome the sterility</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and abstractness of the Enlightenment, and maintain that god can be experienced directly. They</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:229.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">criticize Kant as too universal, and lacking a personal experience of god. They seek a religion of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:243.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">heart - ‘How do I know I'm saved?” “Accept Jesus as your personal savior.” The Great Awakening has</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:257.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">arrived.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:226.97px;top:444.19px" class="cls_007"><span class="cls_007">Caravaggio - The Pietist Schoolman</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:458.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1687 Newton proves much previous Aristotelian ‘science’ wrong, thereby diminishing the role of God in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:472.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the universe; the scientific revolution has begun.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:295.37px;top:667.06px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.29px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">56</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:44912px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background057.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:289.73px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Skepticism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1690 Locke - The first fruits of the Enlightenment: universal human reason, freedom from religious</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">authority, superstition, even religion itself. Locke proposes a "reasonable" christianity, a "natural</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religion" based in reason, though accepting intuitive, self-evident principles.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1739 Hume is an Empiricist (knowledge is founded on sense perception), and a critic of religion, who</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">questions whether one’s senses can confirm natural religion. He shows the limits of knowledge:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">argument from design is faulty because its cause (God) is not proportional to the observed effect (the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">world). Religion has its origin in human psychology, especially in fear and desire for power.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1767 Voltaire proposes Deism (belief in a non-interventionist supreme being), and gives a scathing</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">critique of traditional Christianity. Opponents claim that without God, morality would collapse.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1770 Diderot, an atheist materialist: ‘Religious explanations cannot be rationally defended.’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:231.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1774 Unitarianism is a movement named for its belief that the God is one person, as opposed to a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:245.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Trinity. Unitarians believe that Jesus was inspired in his moral teachings, and he is a savior, but he was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:259.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not himself a god. Unitarianism also rejects the doctrines of original sin, predestination, Biblical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:273.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inerrancy, and punishment in an eternal hell.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:289.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1774 Romanticism: In reaction to the implications of the Enlightenment, Romantics emphasize one’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:303.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spontaneous, emotional, creative side; the artistic-contemplative connection to nature; a mystical union</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:317.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with the divine that produces works of art beyond the reach of reason.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:333.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1780 Thomas Jefferson considers the teachings of Jesus as having "the most sublime and benevolent code</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:347.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of morals which has ever been offered to man," yet he holds that the pure teachings of Jesus appear to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:361.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have been appropriated by some of Jesus' early followers, resulting in a Bible that contains both</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:375.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"diamonds" of wisdom and the "dung" of ancient political agenda. Jefferson used certain passages of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:389.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">New Testament to compose </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jefferson_Bible">The Life and Morals of Jesus of Nazareth</A> (the "Jefferson Bible"), which</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:403.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">stressed his moral message without any </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miracle">miracles</A> or reference to his divinity.</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:419.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1781 Kant generates his "critical philosophy" -</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:419.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and happiness don't coincide; hence we must</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:433.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">knowledge is based on the mind's active</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:433.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">postulate god and immortality, so that we have an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:448.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">organization of sense experience. We cannot</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:448.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">infinite amount of time to progress toward virtue.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:462.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">experience the thing in itself, cannot know god,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:462.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Without these postulates, we would despair.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:475.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and so we must postulate god. All knowledge</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:475.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Happiness and virtue will ultimately converge,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:490.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">originates in sense experience organized by innate</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:490.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but believers need a church to support and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:504.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ideas - we can deduce a rational faith through</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:504.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">encourage them.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:518.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">regulative ideas (god, world, self) which bring</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:532.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unity at the highest level to experience. To act</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:546.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">morally is to ignore all other incentives (emotion,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:560.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">self-interest) and to bind oneself to a universal</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:574.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">moral law in the form of the categorical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:588.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">imperative - the principle of an act may be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:602.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">universalized. To act morally is to act</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:616.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">autonomously, but our desire for happiness works</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:630.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">subconsciously as we are seduced by "radical evil,"</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">which always subverts our moral action, so virtue</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:295.37px;top:658.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.77px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">57</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:45714px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background058.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:289.13px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1807 Hegel</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:76.34px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“History is the process whereby the Absolute Spirit empties itself into creation, and humans evolve</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from self-consciousness to god-consciousness.” He feels Kant is unable to reconcile the subjective and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">objective and Romantic emphasis on feeling and emotion. Kant is static, yet reality evolves. His</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inability to know the "thing in itself" is a mere stage in the growth of consciousness. Hegel is an idealist</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(reality consists of ideas), so while Kant's idealism is subjective, Hegel’s is absolute - we can know</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">through our rational faculties. Spirit begins as undifferentiated, then successively differentiates until</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">through dialectic achieving the reconciliation of Spirit. Religion is a social phenomenon to show people</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">who they are; Protestantism makes priests of all believers, so that the divine is found not in church but</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:195.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in the state, and religion is eventually superseded by philosophy.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:359.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1810 Schleiermacher - Piety gives us experience of reality and our absolute dependence on god. Religion</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:373.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is a separate irreducible sphere of life; it is the sense and taste for the infinite, feeling part of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:387.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">universe, in which we lose our sense of oneness and become one with the universe.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:403.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1835 David Strauss’ book The Life of Jesus posits that in Scripture people wrote a mythical rather</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:417.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">historical text - true as myth, not as history. The gospels are true, even if they didn’t happen; they are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:431.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">parables meant to communicate a religious truth, just as Parson Weems invented the story of George</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:445.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Washington and the cherry tree.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:612.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1840 Emerson stresses defying convention and looking within for the unique insight (the Quaker Inner</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:626.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Light) granted to each individual, that no one else can find for one. "As men's prayers are a disease of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the will, so are their creeds a disease of the intellect" (Self-Reliance, 1841).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:295.37px;top:656.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.65px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">58</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:46516px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background059.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:285.53px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Kierkegaard</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1841 Ludwig Feuerbach: “Religion prevents one from grappling with the reality of life.” God is a creation</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the human imagination; we attribute to God crucial aspects of our own humanity, alienating</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ourselves from our true essence, masking and exacerbating fundamental forces of alienation and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">suffering; we must overcome belief in God and recover our own essence. Reality is ultimately material;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hegel's highest realities (self-consciousness, reason, and spirit) are aspects of humanity alienated by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religion. We must renounce a god that requires exclusive faith commitments that separate us from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">other human beings, to come to a sense of ourselves again.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1843 Kierkegaard:  Abraham's killing of Isaac is a teleological suspension of the ethical by the spiritual, like</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that of Iphigenia, a murder of innocence for the greater good. His Night of Infinite Resignation</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">stresses giving up this world in favor of the next (pandering to the hope of immortality). He posits</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faith by virtue of the Absurd - a leap of faith, but not blind faith - a human heart risking all, without</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">justification, trusting in God's love. He attacks</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">modern efforts to make Christianity reasonable;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">faith is only realized in passionate commitment.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Faith is the struggle of a lifetime, an encounter</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with the creative source of life. Abraham's</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">sacrifice of Isaac is murder, an act of faith, an act</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:323.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of infinite resignation, which views things of this</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">world as unimportant compared with things</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">eternal. Abraham has faith through the Absurd</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">idea that he will get Isaac back. Kierkegaard's</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:379.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">paradox: God's is transcendent; faith itself is a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:393.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gift from god, that reason cannot grasp, so reason</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">resents it, and because of sin cannot accept it.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:421.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">An encounter with Jesus the teacher grants us the condition of acceptance and salvation. Religious truth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:436.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">comes to us from outside; salvation is not available except through Jesus. As sinners, we don't want to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:449.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">see it; our reason is offended, but God is absolutely different, while reason wants to domesticate God.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:463.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Reason must recognize and accept its limits and surrender to the paradox. [Yet faith is likewise bound</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:478.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">up with pride, and refuses to recognize a law outside itself - reason. Also, as long as we’re surrendering</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:492.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to paradoxes, how do we know which one? Doesn’t Islam or any cult leader make exactly the same claim</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:506.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that since reason can't arrive at their predetermined conclusion, we must abandon reason and “take the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">leap of faith and trust that God will catch you”? Of course, our “God-given” reason recoils at anything</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">so monstrous as murdering one’s own child.]</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:550.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1844 The YMCA is founded in London to put Christian principles into practice by developing a healthy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:564.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">"body, mind, and spirit."</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:47318px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background060.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:240.29px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">John Henry Newman and Marx</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1845 John Henry Newman defends the authority of the church. One can know God only through self-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">denial and obedience, to which the Church is an indispensable guide. World history is moved by divine</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">activity in a continuing revelation. Catholics must trust that the church is infallible.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1847 Horace Bushnell: Doctrines of sin and salvation cannot be dismissed; one must read the bible as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">inspiration and a poetic form of life, as different branches pointing at the same truth; doctrines evolve.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1848 Marx Religion is a false consciousness by which people delude themselves to cope with oppression; it</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is a psychological and social, rather than divine, phenomenon. Feuerbach's reversal of Hegel is an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">important step, but Feuerbach is mistaken in his view that the power of thought can change human life;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Marx has an entirely materialistic interpretation: human emancipation will occur when we overcome</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the split between citizenship and civil society. The Communist Manifesto is issued in 1848, as anti-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">monarchical revolutions rock Europe, proclaiming the need for a proletarian revolution from below.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The movement of history is not a matter of thought, but of human productive activity. Philosophers</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">interpret the world; the point is to change it. Feuerbach thought of religion as a form of illness, splitting</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">us in two; for Marx, religion is only a symptom - the sickness is inequality and oppression; religion is a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">palliative, the opium of the people, to make us forget how miserable we are, a false consciousness shaped</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">by forces that it hides from itself. We must look below the surface to social material biological dynamics.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1852 Ritschl is a spokesman for liberal Protestants</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and modernist Catholics: there is no conflict</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:341.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">between modernism and religion; doctrines are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:355.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mere poetic expressions of religious experience.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:369.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Ritschl, a Kantian considers Jesus the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:383.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">embodiment of ethical calling; divine grace is a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:397.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spiritual freedom that makes moral action possible</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in the context of Christian tradition. Jesus’ ethical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">work justifies the Christian community.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Salvation can come only through Jesus;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:454.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Protestantism is the consummation of God's plan.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:469.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1865 The Salvation Army is founded to bring salvation to the poor, destitute, and hungry by meeting</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:484.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">both their "physical and spiritual needs,” running charity shops, and operating shelters for the homeless.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1869 Modern “Christianity”: In order to appeal to a broader spectrum, and especially vibrant masculinity,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religions compromise core values - "turning the other cheek" is replaced by a muscular embrace of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">military expansionism; serving the poor is replaced by "Acres of Diamonds."</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:544.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1869 Ultramontanists - Catholic Anti-modernists give greater authority to the Pope. In 1854 Pius IX</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:558.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">declares the teaching of the Immaculate Conception without consulting bishops; in 1864 he publishes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Syllabus of Errors condemning secularization and political liberalism; in 1869 the First Vatican</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Council declares him infallible based on Mt 16:18. In 1870, in answer to threats from secularization,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Aquinas is declared to be the foundation of dogma.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:616.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1870 Bruno Bauer: Jews will be emancipated only when religion is abolished; the state offers us freedom</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:630.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in the abstract: Paul says there are neither slave nor free, neither male nor female, yet he supported</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">slavery and subordination of women; the state makes us equal as citizens, yet allows deep inequalities;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:658.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">consciousness mystifies and ritualizes the social origins of alienation and domination.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:674.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.33px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">60</span></div>

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background061.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:236.09px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Liberal Protestant and Nietzsche</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1875 Liberal Protestants - roots in Unitarian revolt against orthodox Calvinism - come into mainstream</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of US Protestantism; adapt religious ideas to modern culture (reconcile Christianity w/science); reject</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">biblical literalism; stress ethical teachings of the Bible; ally w/“social gospel;” and urban revivalists;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">optimistic trust in community, focus on salvation and personal growth; accept evolution through</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“natural selection,” rejecting the “dogma of special creations.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1879 Christian Scientists are founded by Mary Baker Eddy for those who believe faith can heal any illness.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1882 Nietzsche “God is dead!” True World theologies are debunked. True World theology (the idea</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that paradise exists, but not here) is of three types: Temporal (this world is the only reality, but is being</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">guided and will be transformed in the future, yielding philosophies of history, like that of Marx),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Monistic (individuals are identical to the universe, as in the Upanishads and transcendentalism and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zen), and Eternal (beside this earthly reality is a parallel Christian/Muslim/Buddhist heaven/hell).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:244.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">For those who have cast off these psychological crutches, life is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:258.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">suddenly unhinged and seems meaningless. Mere material</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:272.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prosperity cannot solve the dilemma of meaning in life. People</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:286.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">need the True World theories to protect them from the harsh</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:300.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">realities of this world. Without them they sink into nihilism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:316.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">According to Nietzsche, the conclusion that life is meaningless is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:330.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mistaken: nihilism must be transcended. There are two types of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:344.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">nihilists: Passive Nihilists, for whom the rejection of the myth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:358.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of an afterlife shatters their sense of order in the universe.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:372.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Disoriented and searching for some meaning beyond narrow</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:386.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">self-interest, they are often sucked into mass political</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:400.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">movements. Active Nihilists, however, having realized the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:414.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">death of God, search within themselves for their unique</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:428.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">meaning to life (their Will to Power); they “become who they</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:442.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">are,” embrace adversity, and say “Yes!” to life.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:258.29px;top:459.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The first step is to overcome the fear of non-conformity</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:472.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(like Emerson’s dictum, “Society punishes non-conformity.”) and laziness. A person requires an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:487.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">organizing idea. The specifics are not important, but one must look within to find one’s passion,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:501.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">one’s unique goal, one’s Will to Power. Adversity, far from being a cause for despair, is the very</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:515.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">stuff of growth and life. Lasting happiness arises not through material wealth, or through following</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:529.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">a religious phantasm, but only through struggle to achieve one’s self-appointed goal.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:545.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1883 Wellhausen develops the documentary hypothesis, a historical-critical method whereby the Bible is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:559.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shown to be a text written and often edited by humans at various times.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:575.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1900 20th century New Atheists criticize the violence, irrationality, and intolerance of religion.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:591.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1902 Capitalist Christianity: "Coal mining is a business, not a religious, sentimental, or academic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:605.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">proposition. The rights and interests of the laboring man will be protected and cared for not by the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:619.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">labor agitators, but by the Christian men, to whom God in His infinite wisdom has given control of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:633.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">property interests of the country." George F. Baer, President Philadelphia and Redding Coal and Iron</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:647.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Co.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:663.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.77px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">61</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:48922px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background062.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:198.98px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fundamentalism - Knees jerk, heads find the sand</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:81.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1859 Darwin's Origin of the Species claims the world is far older than the Bible allows, and rejects history</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:95.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">guided by God; natural selection contradicts the Bible claim that God created each species.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1874 What is Darwinism Charles Hodge attacks evolution as atheistic; he and others form the core of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Princeton Theology, a fundamentalist doctrine;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:74.18px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1910-1915 AC Dixon The Fundamentals expresses opposition to modernism and higher criticism (the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">documentary hypothesis), and tries to make biblical theology an empiricist philosophy.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In Fundamentalism, three streams converge: those</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:183.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Evangelicalism (Great Awakening),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:197.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Dispensationalism (apocalypticism), and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Princeton Theology (Biblical inerrancy), to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">assert five fundamental beliefs:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:336.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1) inerrancy of the Bible,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:336.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2) the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biblical_literalism">literal nature of the biblical accounts,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:345.67px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">especially regarding Christ's miracles and the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:345.67px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genesis_creation_narrative">Creation account in Genesis,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:336.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3) the virgin birth of Christ,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:336.65px;top:309.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4) the bodily resurrection and physical return</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:345.67px;top:323.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Christ, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:336.65px;top:337.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">5) the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substitutionary_atonement">substitutionary atonement</A> of Christ on</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:345.67px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the cross.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In socio-political terms, fundamentalism reflects dismay over: the loss of the old religion-based Anglo-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:379.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Saxon order; the movement from an agrarian to an urban society; immigration by non-white, non-</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:393.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Protestants; higher criticism poking holes in the Bible; the collapse of western values during World</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:407.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">War I; the rise of unions; the rise of women; the rise of minorities; and the spread of secondary schools</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:421.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">exposing children to secular ideas and religious doubt.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1915 Anger and dismay at modernism is channeled into the reborn political wing of the Fundamentalist</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">movement, the Ku Klux Klan.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:468.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1916 Karl Barth’s Epistle to the Romans: The brutality of World War I causes a loss of confidence in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:482.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">modernism, and emphasizes God's transcendence. Barth agrees with Feuerbach that religion is ‘people</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:496.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">talking about people.’ Barth prefers revelation - confession, acknowledgement of god's saving message.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:510.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Much influenced by K, Barth asserts that God cannot be known, that religion is ultimately disbelief,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:524.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that religion never gets beyond man to God, that religion is justification of ourselves, that theology is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:538.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">anthropology, that one should be suspicious of religion, that we should allow God to reach us through</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:552.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">revelation, taken on faith. But trying to defend this confession is to acknowledge that humans can judge</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:566.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and explain God (uh-oh); one must read the Bible as the witness of God's revelation. On the left, he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:580.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">rejects Schleiermacher’s transcendence; and on the right, he rejects biblical inerrancy and total</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:594.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">depravity. The bases of faith, however, he considers a priori.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:610.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1919 Prohibition passes, a predominantly Fundamentalist cause.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:626.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
