<div style="position:absolute;left:269.81px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">What it’s all about?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1920 Freud: Religion is an illusion that helps us repress fundamental conflicts at the heart of our psychic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">life, the expression of our repressed desires in coded ways, originating in an Oedipal complex, with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">simultaneous love and hate for the Father. God is a form of wish fulfillment, a Father to whom we can</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">express our love and who will forgive us for our hate; that is, our sin. Religion is a false consciousness</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hiding conflict between amoral pleasure and reality; it is a negotiation between the id and ego; it is a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mass neurosis. Consciousness is shaped by repression of desire; civilization is built on coercion and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">renunciation. Religion is an effect of repression and the inability of humans to confront unavoidable</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">psychic conflict.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1923 The New Geology by Fundamentalist George</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">McCready Price: the creation of the Earth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">occurred on a Tuesday in 4004 BCE.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1925The Butler Act bans teaching evolution; hence</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Scopes Trial, during which William Jennings</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Bryan attacks the “oligarchy of scientists.” Bryan</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is humiliated on the stand and dies a week later.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1920’s School textbook publishers self-censor</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">controversial science to suit Fundamentalism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:329.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1928 Southern and Midwestern Democrats’ reject</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:343.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Al Smith for being wet, Catholic New Yorker.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:359.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1945 Dietrich Bonhoeffer, an advocate of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:373.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“religionless christianity,” is executed by the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:387.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Nazis. In the growing secularization after the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:401.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">death of God, religion ceases to play a significant</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:415.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">role, with increasing separation of church and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:429.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">state, decreasing numbers of worshippers, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:443.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the individualization of religion.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:460.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1947 Carl Henry The Uneasy Conscience of the Modern Fundamentalist: reasserts biblical infallibility: God's</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:474.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">revelations are the source of all truth, moral absolutes; all human thought must begin with</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:488.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">presuppositions that cannot be proven but can be rationally defended.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:504.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1951 Paul Tillich Reactions to Barth: Barth overlooks the inherent linkage between humans and God:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:518.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">people are threatened by meaninglessness.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1953 Ludwig Wittgenstein, a traditionalist, posits that trust and community ground all forms of life,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:548.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">though he has suspicion of particular beliefs and practices rather than religion in general. He asserts</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:562.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conservative politics and fundamentalist religion as the right path.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:578.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1957 Sputnik alarms the US out of its narcotizing religiosity and denial of science.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:594.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1961 Flood Geology asserts that Noah’s flood caused geological layers.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:610.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1962 Engel v Vitale bans school prayer.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:626.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1963 Faced with the possible Soviet supremacy in space, the US updates its education with modern</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:640.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">science textbooks.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:205.94px;top:49.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Religion of Politics or Politics of Religion</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.38px;top:65.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1967 Liberation theology brings out the political relevance of theology and rejects generalism; the church</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:79.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is not a fortress, but part of the city. The church is too closely associated with local elites; religion is used</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:93.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as an opiate for the poor. James Cone in A Black Theology of Liberation stresses the links between</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:107.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">political and social liberation and God's work on the one hand, and complicity of the churches in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:121.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">oppressive sexism, racism, economic exploitation, wide gap between rich and poor, and Marxist views</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:135.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the influence of material conditions upon consciousness on the other. Critics of this view cite a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:149.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">conflation of political liberation and Christian salvation.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:163.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mary Daly: Liberation theology is a response to poverty, the evils of colonialism, and the failure of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:177.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">first world to spark development.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:191.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Oscar Romero: Christian faith ought not to isolate us from, but rather immerse us in the world.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:207.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1970 Hal Lindsay’s The Late, Great Planet Earth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:221.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">suggests 1988 as the time of the Rapture.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:237.62px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1973 Roe v Wade legalizes abortion.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:253.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1974 Paul Ricoeur sees Barth's suspicion of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">religion's false comforts deepening the language</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of faith. He seeks suspicion to destroys idols and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:295.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">create space to hear the word of God.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:311.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1983 Rowan Williams: We need to recover</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">elements of pre-modern traditions; ethics cannot</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">be based in human reason; revelation, not reason</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is the shaping force in life. On Christian Theology</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">acknowledges suspicion as a spiritual exercise: if</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">we start from the human, we can't arrive at God;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">revelation allows us to break out of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:409.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">liberal/fundamentalist dichotomy.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1968 Butler Act is ruled unconstitutional; Fundamentalists demand “Equal Time” to teach Creationism.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:442.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1980 Ronald Reagan champions Fundamentalism with the slogan, “Let’s Make America Great Again!”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:458.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1987 The Supreme Court determines that Creation Science is religious, strikes down Equal Time; the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fundamentalists now promote Intelligent Design.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:488.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1988 88 Reasons why the Rapture will occur in 1988 by Edgar Whisenant. He is wrong</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:504.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1991 Gianni Vattimo : Secularization is a purification of religion, a trait of authentic religious experience.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:520.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1991 Stephen Carter The Culture of Disbelief: Religions are mutually exclusive: extra ecclesia nulla salus;</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:534.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The ideas of “God's chosen people” breeds intolerance. How can we function in a religiously diverse</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:548.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">society? Secularism - people from all faiths or no faith engage on a level playing field. Strong secularism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:562.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">holds that public discourse should be free of religious language, but in that case, religion might be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:576.31px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">trivialized - the price of the compromise reached by the Founding Fathers. The US has had for the past</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:590.35px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">50 years a legal secularism in which the public sphere is strictly secular and religion deemed irrelevant to</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:650.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2000 Plantinga: Belief can be rationally justified without evidence if this belief serves as a properly basic</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:51328px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background065.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:274.73px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The End of Faith:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2004 Sam Harris asserts that religion is irrational,  causes violence, and refuses to acknowledge the truth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of other religions. Harris is critical of the </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_right">Christian right</A> in politics in the United States, blaming them</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for the political focus on "pseudo-problems like gay marriage." He is also critical of </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_Christianity">liberal</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_Christianity">Christianity</A><span class="cls_003">—as represented, for instance, by the theology of <A HREF="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Tillich">Paul Tillich</A>—which he argues claims to</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">base its beliefs on the Bible despite actually being influenced by secular modernity. He further states</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">that in so doing liberal Christianity provides rhetorical cover to fundamentalists. He proposes</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">spirituality without religion.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:300.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2010 Jeffrey Stout Democracy and Tradition supports a weaker form of secularism that he terms</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:314.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“secularization” whereby religious people need not relinquish their beliefs; people with different</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:328.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">backgrounds can come together in constructive interaction.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:344.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2016 Fundamentalists overwhelmingly support Donald Trump for President, not for his character or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:358.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">personal beliefs, but because they feel he will put them back in charge of the culture. David Brody, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:373.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">host of “Faith Nation” on the Christian Broadcasting Network: “Does Mr. Trump have moral failings?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:386.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Yes. Critics will suggest a hypocrisy coming from evangelical leaders who are quick to denounce the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:400.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ethical failings of others who don’t have an “R” next to their name. But the goal of evangelicals has</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:415.01px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">always been winning the larger battle over control of the culture, not to get mired in the moral failings</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:429.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of each and every candidate. For evangelicals, voting in the macro is the moral thing to do, even if the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:443.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">candidate is morally flawed. Evangelicals have tried the “moral” candidate before.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:290.93px;top:461.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:309.29px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">65</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:52130px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background066.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:189.62px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Historical vs. the Mythical Jesus - Authentication</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:329.81px;top:87.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">So what most likely really happened two</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:101.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thousand years ago? There are numerous stories</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:115.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">about Jesus, some more credible than others.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Those events which more likely occurred must be</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">carefully sifted out from the miraculous</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mythology invented by his followers inspired by</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the “Holy Spirit.”  The sources within 100 years</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of Jesus’ death from which all the information we</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have on Jesus are as follows:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:215.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The non-Christian documentation of Jesus’ life is very slim: only two short Roman references:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:231.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Pliny the Younger (112 CE) - Ltr #10 to Trajan: “Christians are a pestiferous group who worship Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:245.57px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">as a god; how should I deal with them?”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:261.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Tacitus Annals (115 CE) - “The burning of Rome in 64 CE is blamed on Christians, who are the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:275.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hatred of the human race, followers of Jesus, who was crucified by Pilate.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:291.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and one contemporary Jewish source:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:307.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Philo (20 BCE-50 CE) - never mentions Jesus.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:323.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Flavius Josephus (37-100 CE) mentions Jesus, with possible emendation by later Christian scribes -</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">18:3:3 “Jesus a doer of wonders, the Messiah, rose from the dead.”</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In Scripture, Jesus is mentioned in Paul, Acts, non-canonical sources, and the Gospels:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:369.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Paul, who never met Jesus and seems not to have been familiar with his teachings, appears to know only</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:383.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the following about Jesus: he was born of a woman (Gal 4:4), Jewish (Gal 4:4), had brothers (1 Cor</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:397.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">9:5), one of whom was named James (Gal 1), ministered principally to Jews (Rom 15:8), was betrayed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:411.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(1 Cor 11), held the Last Supper (1Cor 11), and was crucified. Of Jesus’ teachings Paul records only that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:425.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christians should not get divorced and ought to pay preachers, but Paul never cites Jesus’ teachings in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:439.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">defense of doctrine.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:455.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Acts mentions him only in 1:1-8, where Jesus appears, commands the apostles to stay in Jerusalem,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:469.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">evades a question on restoring the kingdom of Israel, then disappears into a cloud.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:486.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Non-canonical Scriptural sources of stories about Jesus abound, such as the Gospels of Thomas, Peter,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and numerous others. These are useful, however, only in reflecting what the early Christian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">community might have thought about Jesus. They have little authenticity regarding Jesus’ actual life.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:530.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">So we must rely largely upon the Gospels and try to distinguish the Historical Jesus from the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:544.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mythological Jesus. Unfortunately, the canonical books of the New Testament have been tampered</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:558.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with, from the addition of nine verses to the gospel of Mark, to John’s manipulation of the day of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">crucifixion to coincide with the killing of the lambs, to the doctored text forced on Erasmus to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">document the teaching of the Trinity, to fraudulent Epistles of Paul and the Deutero-Pauline Epistles,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to the “gospels” of Peter, Thomas, Judas, Mary, and a legion of others. Though the motivations of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:614.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">these forgeries and creative manipulations of fact were most probably pious, they only cloud the facts of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:628.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the life of Jesus.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:293.93px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.33px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">66</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:52932px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background067.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:159.62px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Criteria for Distinguishing Genuine Details from the Life of Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Fortunately, there are criteria available to try to cull the factual from the fantastic. Many of the stories</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">attributed to Jesus are inconsistent, illogical, and unsubstantiated. So how can we know what really</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">happened? To the usual standards of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Multiple Attestation: Being noted in more than one independent source (confers increasing plausibility),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Dissimilarity:  When an entry is unlikely to have been added by zealous Christian wishing to embellish</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the image of Jesus (this too lends increased plausibility), and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:173.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Contextual credibility: Whether actions or words fit 1</span><span class="cls_010">st</span><span class="cls_003"> century Palestine (lack of such credibility</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:187.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">decreases plausibility),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:203.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">I would add miracles/dreams/angels (decreasing plausibility) prophetic fulfillment (decreasing</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:217.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">plausibility), and lack of witness except the “Holy Spirit” (decreasing plausibility). These last three</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:231.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">criteria are my own, for which I offer the following rationale:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:247.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Miracles/dreams/angels: No, Virginia, there is no Santa Claus. The understandable tendency of people</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:261.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">to perpetuate myth must be let go of to find the truth of Jesus’ life. Miracles, that is, physical</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:275.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">impossibilities, do not occur in this universe. There are phenomena (events in the cursus communis</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:289.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">naturae) that we don’t yet understand, so perhaps Jesus knew some secret way to turn water into wine,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:303.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">but it is highly improbable. “Magic” is a skill that one can learn from Penn and Teller or David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:317.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Copperfield. The “miracles” of “Jesus as</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:331.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wonder-worker” are likewise either reasonable</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:345.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(casting out demons is credible because demonic</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:359.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">possession might be an entirely psychological</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:328.01px;top:373.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">phenomenon), exaggerations (probable in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:387.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">case of the loaves and fishes), deceptions, or figments of the imagination (that is, stories inspired</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:401.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">after the fact by the ‘Holy Spirit’). Jesus is like a Christmas tree, a noble pine burdened with all</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:415.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">manner of legendary material added like tinsel to promote belief in him. Ought one not to consider</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:429.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christian miracles as one considers the miracles of other faiths? Just as George Washington did not</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:443.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">cut down an apple tree, nor is there an Easter bunny, nor does Santa Claus fly in a sleigh from the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:457.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">North Pole, nor is there a tooth fairy, these tales of impossible acts simply did not happen. Nor</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">was Jesus alone in performing miracles; even Simon Magus was supposedly able to fly.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:488.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Prophetic fulfillment: This is another red flag for one seeking the real story. After Jesus’ sudden,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:502.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">shocking, and tragic demise, his followers frantically scoured the Old Testament for any reference</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:516.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">they could find, or manufacture, referring to the Messiah and then created stories to write those</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:530.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">references back into his life. Biblical sources were misinterpreted, taken out of context, or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:544.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">mistranslated to provide “proof” of Jesus’ Messianic role. Interestingly, Jesus didn’t even fulfill the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:558.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">basic requirement of the Messianic mission, that of freeing Israel from foreign domination, but</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:572.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">followers were expecting a Messiah, so they stretched Isaiah 53 and created stories to fit all</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophecies of the Messiah, and even invented a few (“He shall be called a Nazarene.”).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:602.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Witness of the Holy Spirit. Events to which no reliable human witness may be attributed are</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:616.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">expected to be accepted on the grounds that the Holy Spirit inspired the evangelist. We may give</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:630.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">no more credence to such stories than we do to Milton’s Paradise Lost, Dante’s Divine Comedy, or</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Iliad. The Holy Spirit here is merely another avatar of the poet’s Muse.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:284.93px;top:660.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:308.81px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">67</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:53734px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">
<div style="position:absolute;left:0px;top:0px">
<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background068.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:244.37px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Life of the Historical Jesus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This is as much as we may assert with a high probability of accuracy:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:99.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus was born in Nazareth (a backward village so insignificant it is not mentioned once in the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:113.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Hebrew Scriptures or Josephus) to Mary and Joseph (Joseph is never heard from again) around 4</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">BCE, and had siblings - both brothers and sisters (Mk 3</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Mark-6-3/">:3)</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He was born and raised as a Jew, though the area of Galilee had recently been forcibly converted to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Judaism by Aristobolus I in 104 BCE, so the Jewish genealogy of Jesus’ family is subject to question.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus was most probably trained to be a tekton - carpenter, or construction worker of some sort, and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">seems to have been drawn to the apocalyptic teaching of his “cousin” (Luke 1:36, 57-60), John the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Baptist. Indeed, in Matthew, Jesus’ first recorded preaching (4:17 “Repent: for the kingdom of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">heaven is at hand.”) is a direct quote from John, and Jesus seems to have wanted to fulfill John’s</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">expectation of a Messiah. He began his ministry in his native Galilee, but was not well received</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">either by his family (Mk 3:21, Mk 3:30, John 7:5), or the neighboring towns of Galilee (Mk 6:1, Lk</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:28, Mt 11:20 (=Lk10:13). Though the chief Galilean cities of Cepherus and Tiberius were within</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">walking distance, Jesus is never recorded as having gone there. He was a prophet without honor</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Mk 6:3), who had no home (Mt 8, Lk 9, John 15:18).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:299.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Much in the mold of Isaiah, he shared John’s contempt for the Pharisees (Jews who emphasize</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:313.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">scrupulous adherence to the letter of the Law, often overlooking its spirit) and Sadducees (elitist</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:327.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">priests of the Temple in Jerusalem, who collaborated with the Roman authorities), and was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:341.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">concerned for the long-suffering common people.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:357.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Around 30 CE, he went to Jerusalem at Passover, apparently to cement his reputation as a prophet</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:371.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and to make his Apocalyptic point, perhaps even to incite an armed uprising. He overturned the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:385.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">tables of money-changers and, as intended, attracted the unfavorable attention of the Jewish and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:399.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Roman authorities by disrupting Temple activities and preaching the imminent revolution.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:415.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He was betrayed by his disciple Judas, who,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:429.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">perhaps in an attempt to force Jesus to take</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:443.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">some miraculous action, likely told the Roman</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:457.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">authorities that he had claimed to be the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:472.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Messiah and future ruler of Palestine. Jesus was</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:486.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">arrested (while with his band of armed</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“zealots”), tried by Pontius Pilate, crucified,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and probably died on the cross, though Josephus</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">tells of two men who survived crucifixion. As</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:542.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">for his “resurrection,” he was most likely buried</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:556.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">in a mass grave, as was customary for those</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:124.94px;top:570.43px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Grünewald Crucifixion 1512</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:570.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">crucified for treason.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:586.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">His stunned and terrified followers, none of whom were directly present at his death, settled on Jesus’</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:600.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">identity as the (redefined) Messiah. To bolster their claim, they scoured the Hebrew Scriptures for</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:614.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">references to the Messiah and rewrote Jesus’ story to “fulfill” the Scriptural references. Fifty to eighty</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:628.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">years after his death, Christian proselytizers formulated their promotional literature into the Gospels.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:293.93px;top:644.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:299.69px;top:699.70px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">68</span></div>
</div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:276.05px;top:49.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus’ Genealogy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:65.28px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">To show the Jewish messianic legitimacy of Jesus, Matthew traces David’s line down to Joseph. The</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:79.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">problem is that Luke also traces Jesus’ genealogy, but his is almost completely different from that of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:93.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Matthew! Most damaging of all for the credibility of this section is the assertion that the Holy Spirit,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:107.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not Joseph, impregnates Mary, so that the whole genealogy to Joseph is pointless! Hence Jesus is NOT</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:121.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">from the line of David, whether or not Joseph is.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:375.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">14 Eliezer</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:171.02px;top:375.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">29 Mattathias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:342.05px;top:375.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">|</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:378.07px;top:375.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">14 Josias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:90.02px;top:389.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">15 Jose</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:171.02px;top:389.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">30 Maath</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:342.05px;top:389.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">|</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:378.07px;top:389.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">15 Jechonias</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Genealogies become important during the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian Captivity. The exiled priestly and</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ruling classes of Judah decide that YHWH</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brought the Babylonians to destroy Jerusalem</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:466.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and the Temple because of marriage to unclean</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:480.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">local women, through whom worship of other</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:494.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">gods spread. Thus, they each have to show their</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:508.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">own genealogical purity by inventing a family</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:522.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">tree that stretches back to David. This rejection</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:536.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of aliens is also the origin of the intense</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:550.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">xenophobia that is still a hallmark of Judaism</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:333.41px;top:564.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">today.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:578.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Another, perhaps even more fundamental, motive for these genealogies is their use in asserting claim to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:592.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the land in Judah lost to the unclean lower classes during the Exile. Still, the root cause for early</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:606.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Christians to assert the Davidic origin of Jesus is the prophecy that the Messiah will spring from</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:620.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">David’s line.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:636.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">It’s interesting to note that Luke’s genealogy lists the father of Salathiel, the king-in-exile during the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:650.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian Captivity, not as Jeconias, the king of Judah before him, but as Neri, an otherwise</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:664.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unknown individual with a  unisex Hebrew name meaning “my candle.”</span></div>

</div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:50%;margin-left:-306px;top:55338px;width:612px;height:792px;border-style:outset;overflow:hidden">

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background070.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:273.05px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The Virgin Birth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:87.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 1:18 Now the birth of Jesus Christ was on this wise: When as his mother Mary was espoused to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:101.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Joseph, before they came together, she was found with child of the Holy Ghost. 1:19 Then Joseph</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:115.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">her husband, being a just man, and not willing to make her a publick example, was minded to put</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:129.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">her away privily. 1:20 But while he thought on these things, behold, the angel of the LORD</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:143.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">appeared unto him in a dream, saying, Joseph, thou son of David, fear not to take unto thee Mary</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:157.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thy wife: for that which is conceived in her is of the Holy Ghost. 1:21 And she shall bring forth a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:171.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">son, and thou shalt call his name JESUS: for he shall save his people from their sins. 1:22 Now all</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">this was done, that it might be fulfilled which was spoken of the Lord by the prophet, saying,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1:23 Behold, a virgin shall be with child, and shall bring forth a son, and they shall call his name</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Emmanuel, which being interpreted is, God with us. (Isa 7:14)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:227.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">1:24 Then Joseph being raised from sleep did as the angel of the Lord had bidden him, and took</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:241.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto him his wife: 1:25 And knew her not till she had brought forth her firstborn son: and he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:255.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">called his name JESUS.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.29px;top:269.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The angel and dream are necessitated by pregnancy</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:283.61px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">out of wedlock. Prophetic fulfillment here is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:297.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">based upon a mistranslation of Isaiah 7:14, which</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:311.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">says, in Hebrew, “the young woman  (alma) is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:325.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">with child,”  not, as erroneously translated into</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:339.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Greek in the Septuagint, “a virgin” (parthenos),</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:353.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and taken entirely out of context. The proper</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:367.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">context of the quote is that at that time Syria</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(Rezin) and Israel (Pekah) are organizing an</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">anti-Assyrian alliance and are threatening to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:409.97px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">replace King Ahaz of Judah if he will not join.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The LORD instructs Isaiah to convince Ahaz</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">not to join the alliance. Isaiah offers a sign that</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:451.99px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the alliance will fail: before the child that the young woman is even now carrying is old enough to eat</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:466.03px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">butter and honey (to know right from wrong), the alliance will fail. This context is clear if one reads the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:480.07px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">preceding and following lines of Isaiah with the above-mentioned correction:</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:500.11px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Is7</span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-3/">:3 Then said the LORD unto Isaiah, Go forth now to meet Ahaz.</A><span class="cls_003">.. <A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-4/">4 And say unto him, Take</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:514.15px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-4/">heed, and be quiet; fear not, neither be fainthearted for the two tails of these smoking firebrands,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:528.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-4/">for the fierce anger of Rezin with Syria, and of the son of Remaliah..</A><span class="cls_003">. <A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-6/">6 Let us go up against</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:542.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-6/">Judah, and vex it, and let us make a breach therein for us, and set a king in the midst of it, even the</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:556.27px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-6/">son of Tabeal: 7 Thus saith the Lord GOD, It shall not stand, neither shall it come to pass..</A><span class="cls_003">. <A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-14/">14</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:570.19px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-14/">Therefore the Lord himself shall give you a sign; Behold, the young woman is with child, and she</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:584.23px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-14/">will bear a son, and shall call his name Immanuel. 15 Butter and honey shall he eat, that he may</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:598.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-15/">know to refuse the evil, and choose the good. 16 For before the child shall know to refuse the evil,</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:612.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003"> </span><A HREF="https://www.kingjamesbibleonline.org/Isaiah-7-16/">and choose the good, the land that thou abhorrest shall be forsaken of both her kings.</A> </div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:632.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">The whole nonsensical myth of Mary conceiving as a virgin is debunked. And they didn’t even name the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:646.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">child Emmanuel! Outrage at this sort of blatant misreading of Scripture was a key point of friction</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.38px;top:660.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">between early Christians and Jews.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:221.69px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">We Three Kings of Orient Are - Not!</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:276.17px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">In a story apparently intended to show the universality of Jesus’ message, Zoroastrian magi (wise men)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:290.21px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(not kings, not three) are led by a star not to the baby Jesus, but to Herod’s palace, where they have to</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:304.25px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ask directions?! Why would the story-teller want the wise men to go to Herod’s palace? Simply in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:318.29px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">order to condemn the chief priests and scribes. Furthermore, Jesus does not fulfill the included</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:332.33px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophecy because he is never ‘governor ruling Israel.’ Also, here Joseph and Mary live in a house in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:346.37px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Bethlehem (no manger), whereas in Luke, they live in Nazareth (in Galilee, outside the range of the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:360.41px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">“census” of Quirinius) and are forced to go to their ancestral home (not required) by the census</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:374.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">(actually a land assessment made in 6 CE) conducted by the newly appointed Imperial Legate,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:388.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Quirinius, supposedly during the reign of Herod the Great (who had died ten years earlier, in 4 BCE).</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:404.45px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 2:1 Now when Jesus was born in Bethlehem of Judaea in the days of Herod the king, behold,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:418.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">there came wise men from the east to Jerusalem, 2:2 Saying, Where is he that is born King of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:432.55px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the Jews? For we have seen his star in the east, and are come to worship him. 2:3 When Herod</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:446.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the king had heard these things, he was troubled, and all Jerusalem with him. 2:4 And when</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:460.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he had gathered all the chief priests and scribes of the people together, he demanded of them</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:474.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">where Christ should be born. 2:5 And they said unto him, In Bethlehem of Judaea: for thus it</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:488.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">is written by the prophet,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:126.02px;top:504.67px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2:6 And thou Bethlehem, in the land of Juda, art not the least among the princes of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:135.02px;top:518.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Juda: for out of thee shall come a Governor, that shall rule my people Israel. (Mic 5:2)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:534.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">2:7 Then Herod, when he had privily called the wise men, enquired of them diligently what</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:548.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">time the star appeared. 2:8 And he sent them to Bethlehem, and said, Go and search</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:562.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">diligently for the young child; and when ye have found him, bring me word again, that I may</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:576.79px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">come and worship him also. 2:9 When they had heard the king, they departed; and, lo, the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:590.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">star, which they saw in the east, went before them, till it came and stood over where the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:604.90px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">young child was. 2:10 When they saw the star, they rejoiced with exceeding great joy. 2:11</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:618.94px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">And when they were come into the house, they saw the young child with Mary his mother,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:632.98px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and fell down, and worshipped him: and when they had opened their treasures, they</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:108.02px;top:647.02px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">presented unto him gifts; gold, and frankincense and myrrh.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:271.49px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">To Nazareth (M)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Matthew has to get Jesus to Nazareth somehow, so why not invent a prophecy, too? There is no Old</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Testament source for “He shall be called a Nazarene.” Herod Archelaus ruled Judea from 4 BCE to 6</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:276.89px;top:448.27px" class="cls_009"><span class="cls_009">King Herod Antipas</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:491.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">dead which sought the young child's life. 2:21 And he arose, and took the young child and his mother,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:505.51px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and came into the land of Israel. 2:22 But when he heard that Archelaus did reign in Judaea in the room</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:533.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">turned aside into the parts of Galilee: 2:23 And he came and dwelt in a city called Nazareth: that it</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:259.01px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">John the Baptist (Mark)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">This has the ring of a true story until 3:14, where John defers to Jesus. Who is baptizing whom here?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Jesus is clearly in the inferior position, so his followers had to invent another ending. John may have</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">been an Essene, the only practitioners of ritual lustrations. John is clearly an Apocalypticist, “The axe is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">laid unto the root of the trees” in the dualist (Zoroastrian) style of Daniel.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:318.65px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 3:1 In those days came John the Baptist,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">preaching in the wilderness of Judaea, 3:2 And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">saying, Repent ye: for the kingdom of heaven is</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:183.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">at hand. 3:3 For this is he that was spoken of by the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:197.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">prophet Esaias, saying, The voice of one crying in</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:211.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">the wilderness, Prepare ye the way of the Lord,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:225.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">make his paths straight. 3:4 And the same John</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:239.54px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">had his raiment of camel's hair, and a leathern</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:267.65px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wild honey. 3:5 Then went out to him Jerusalem,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:281.69px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">and all Judaea, and all the region round about</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:337.73px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">baptism, he said unto them, O generation of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:351.77px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">vipers, who hath warned you to flee from the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:327.65px;top:365.81px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wrath to come?</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:381.89px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">3:8 Bring forth therefore fruits meet for repentance: 3:9 And think not to say within yourselves, We</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:395.93px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">have Abraham to our father: for I say unto you, that God is able of these stones to raise up children unto</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:409.85px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Abraham. 3:10 And now also the axe is laid unto the root of the trees: therefore every tree which</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:423.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">bringeth not forth good fruit is hewn down, and cast into the fire. 3:11 I indeed baptize you with water</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:437.95px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">unto repentance. but he that cometh after me is mightier than I, whose shoes I am not worthy to bear:</span></div>

<img src="5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_id_5fb2c2c4-5f39-11ea-8b25-0cc47a792c0a_files/background074.jpg" width=612 height=792></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:267.29px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Temptation (Mark)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Pure invention. Satan appears in Job as a member of the heavenly court, and as opposing counsel in 1</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Chron 21:1, Ps 109:6, Zech 3:1-2. The explanation of evil in the world had evolved from early Zionist</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Triumphalism - the people of Israel were beneficiaries of the covenant and a descendant of David</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:125.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">would always be on the throne - to Deuteronomism - the belief the Israel was being punished with the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:139.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Babylonian Captivity for impiety of some sort - to  Apocalypticism - a belief based in Zoroastrian</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:153.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">dualism that we live in an age dominated by evil - and the architect of that evil is Satan. This idea</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:167.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">became dominant during the Hellenistic period, when it became evident that no matter how good the</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:181.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">people were, the foreign domination continued.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:394.49px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 4:1 Then was Jesus led up of the spirit into the wilderness to be tempted of the devil. 4:2 And when</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:408.53px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">he had fasted forty days and forty nights, he was afterward an hungred. 4:3 And when the tempter</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:422.59px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">came to him, he said, If thou be the Son of God, command that these stones be made bread. 4:4 But he</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:436.63px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">answered and said, It is written,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:144.14px;top:452.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Man shall not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceedeth out of the mouth</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:302.69px;top:466.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of God.  Deu 8:3</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:482.71px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:5 Then the devil taketh him up into the holy city, and setteth him on a pinnacle of the temple, 4:6</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:496.75px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">And saith unto him, If thou be the Son of God, cast thyself down: for it is written,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:152.18px;top:512.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">He shall give his angels charge concerning thee: and in their hands they shall bear</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:182.30px;top:526.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">thee up, lest at any time thou dash thy foot against a stone. Ps 111:11</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:542.83px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:7 Jesus said unto him, It is written again,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:199.22px;top:558.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Thou shalt not tempt the Lord thy God. Deu 6:16</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:574.87px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:8 Again, the devil taketh him up into an exceeding high mountain, and sheweth him all the kingdoms</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:588.91px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">of the world, and the glory of them; 4:9 And saith unto him, All these things will I give thee, if thou</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:602.98px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">wilt fall down and worship me. 4:10 Then saith Jesus unto him, Get thee hence, Satan: for it is written,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:134.90px;top:619.06px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Thou shalt worship the Lord thy God, and him only shalt thou serve. Deu 6:13</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:635.02px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:11 Then the devil leaveth him, and, behold, angels came and ministered unto him.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:293.93px;top:655.18px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">~~~~~~~</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:264.29px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">To Capernaum (Mk)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Like a chess piece, Jesus is now moved to Capernaum in order to satisfy an obscure “prophecy.” Jesus here</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">embraces John’s gospel, quoting him word for word. The prophecy cited herein is a composite of three</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">versions of the LXX.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:127.34px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 4:12 Now when Jesus had heard that John was cast into prison, he departed into Galilee; 4:13 And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:141.38px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">leaving Nazareth, he came and dwelt in Capernaum, which is upon the sea coast, in the borders of</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:155.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Zabulon and Nephthalim: 4:14 That it might be fulfilled which was spoken by Esaias the prophet,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:169.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">saying,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:185.42px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:15 The land of Zabulon, and the land of Nephthalim, by the way of the sea, beyond Jordan,</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:199.46px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Galilee of the Gentiles; 4:16 The people which sat in darkness saw great light; and to them</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:99.02px;top:213.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">which sat in the region and shadow of death light is sprung up. Isa 9:1-2</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:229.58px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">4:17 From that time Jesus began to preach, and to say, Repent: for the kingdom of heaven is at</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:243.50px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">hand.</span></div>

<div style="position:absolute;left:266.93px;top:67.20px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">First Disciples (Mk)</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:83.30px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Had Jesus met these disciples previously? Either way, their abandonment of their livelihood and father</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:97.22px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">straightway is certainly intended to emphasize the renunciation involved in following Jesus and a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:111.26px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">further blow to family values.</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:72.02px;top:358.37px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">Mt 4:18 And Jesus, walking by the sea of Galilee, saw two brethren, Simon called Peter, and Andrew his</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:372.29px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">brother, casting a net into the sea: for they were fishers. 4:19 And he saith unto them, Follow me, and I</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:386.33px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">will make you fishers of men. 4:20 And they straightway left their nets, and followed him. 4:21 And</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:400.37px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">going on from thence, he saw other two brethren, James the son of Zebedee, and John his brother, in a</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:414.41px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">ship with Zebedee their father, mending their nets; and he called them. 4:22 And they immediately</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:81.02px;top:428.47px" class="cls_003"><span class="cls_003">left the ship and their father, and followed him.</span></div>
